<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about the video game. For the franchise, see <a href="/wiki/Minecraft_(franchise)" title="Minecraft (franchise)"><i>Minecraft</i> (franchise)</a>. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Minecraft_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Minecraft (disambiguation)">Minecraft (disambiguation)</a>.</div>

Hovering over the scene is the Minecraft logo." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/5/51/Minecraft_cover.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="280" class="mw-file-element" <p><i><b>Minecraft</b></i> is a 2011 <a href="/wiki/Sandbox_game" title="Sandbox game">sandbox game</a> developed by <a href="/wiki/Mojang_Studios" title="Mojang Studios">Mojang Studios</a> and originally released in 2009. The game was created by <a href="/wiki/Markus_Persson" title="Markus Persson">Markus "Notch" Persson</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Java_(programming_language)" title="Java (programming language)">Java</a> <a href="/wiki/Programming_language" title="Programming language">programming language</a>. Following several early private testing versions, it was first made public in May 2009 before being fully released on November 18, 2011, with Notch stepping down and <a href="/wiki/Jens_Bergensten" title="Jens Bergensten">Jens "Jeb" Bergensten</a> taking over <a href="/wiki/Video_game_development" title="Video game development">development</a>. <i>Minecraft</i> has become the <a href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_video_games" title="List of best-selling video games">best-selling video game in history</a>, with over 300 million copies sold and nearly 140 million monthly <a href="/wiki/Active_users" title="Active users">active players</a> as of 2023<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Minecraft&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>. It has been ported to several platforms. 
</p><p>In <i>Minecraft</i>, players explore a blocky, pixelated <a href="/wiki/Procedural_generation" title="Procedural generation">procedurally generated</a>, <a href="/wiki/Three-dimensional_space" title="Three-dimensional space">three-dimensional</a> world with virtually infinite terrain. Players can discover and extract raw materials, <a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_video_game_terms#Crafting" title="Glossary of video game terms">craft</a> tools and items, and build structures, <a href="/wiki/Earthworks_(engineering)" title="Earthworks (engineering)">earthworks</a>, and machines. Depending on their chosen <a href="/wiki/Game_mechanics" title="Game mechanics">game mode</a>, players can fight hostile <a href="/wiki/Mob_(video_games)" title="Mob (video games)">mobs</a>, as well as cooperate with or compete against other players in the same world. Game modes include a survival mode (in which players must acquire resources to build in the world and maintain health), creative mode (in which players have unlimited resources and the ability to fly), spectator mode (in which players can fly, go through blocks, and enter the bodies of other players and entities), adventure mode (in which players have to survive without being able to build and place blocks) and hardcore mode (in which the difficulty is set to Hard and dying causes the player to lose their ability to play on that world). The game's large community also offers a wide variety of <a href="/wiki/User-generated_content" title="User-generated content">user-generated content</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Minecraft_modding" title="Minecraft modding">modifications</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minecraft_server" title="Minecraft server">servers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Theme_(computing)#Video_gaming" title="Theme (computing)">skins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Texture_mapping" title="Texture mapping">texture packs</a>, and custom maps, which add new <a href="/wiki/Game_mechanics" title="Game mechanics">game mechanics</a> and possibilities.
</p><p><i>Minecraft</i> has received critical acclaim, winning several awards and being cited by some as one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_video_games_considered_the_best" title="List of video games considered the best">greatest video games ever created</a>; <a href="/wiki/Social_media" title="Social media">social media</a>, <a href="/wiki/Parody" title="Parody">parodies</a>, adaptations, <a href="/wiki/Merchandising" title="Merchandising">merchandise</a>, and the annual <a href="/wiki/Minecon" title="Minecon">Minecon</a> conventions played prominent roles in popularizing the game. The game has also been used in educational environments to teach <a href="/wiki/Chemistry" title="Chemistry">chemistry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Computer-aided_design" title="Computer-aided design">computer-aided design</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Computer_science" title="Computer science">computer science</a>. In 2014, Mojang and the <i>Minecraft</i> intellectual property were purchased by <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a> for <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$2.5</span> billion. Several spin-offs have also been made, including <i><a href="/wiki/Minecraft:_Story_Mode" title="Minecraft: Story Mode">Minecraft: Story Mode</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Minecraft_Earth" title="Minecraft Earth">Minecraft Earth</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Minecraft_Dungeons" title="Minecraft Dungeons">Minecraft Dungeons</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Minecraft_Legends" title="Minecraft Legends">Minecraft Legends</a></i>. In addition, a live-action film of <a href="/wiki/Minecraft_(film)" title="Minecraft (film)">the same name</a> is scheduled for a theatrical release in 2025.
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886046785">.mw-parser-output .toclimit-2 .toclevel-1 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-3 .toclevel-2 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-4 .toclevel-3 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-5 .toclevel-4 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-6 .toclevel-5 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-7 .toclevel-6 ul{display:none}</style><div class="toclimit-3"><meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" /></div>

//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></span></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a href="/wiki/Special:EditPage/Minecraft" title="Special:EditPage/Minecraft">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>&#32;in this section. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.<br /><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22Minecraft%22">"Minecraft"</a>&#160;–&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22Minecraft%22+-wikipedia&amp;tbs=ar:1">news</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22Minecraft%22&amp;tbs=bkt:s&amp;tbm=bks">newspapers</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22Minecraft%22+-wikipedia">books</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22Minecraft%22">scholar</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22Minecraft%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on">JSTOR</a></span></small></span>  <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">January 2024</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><i>Minecraft</i> is a <a href="/wiki/3D_computer_graphics" title="3D computer graphics">3D</a> <a href="/wiki/Sandbox_game" title="Sandbox game">sandbox game</a> that has no required goals to accomplish, allowing players a large amount of freedom in choosing how to play the game.<sup id="cite_ref-IGN_review_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IGN_review-25">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> However, there is an <a href="/wiki/Achievement_(video_games)" title="Achievement (video games)">achievement</a> system,<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> known as "advancements" in the <i>Java Edition</i> of the game, "<a href="/wiki/PlayStation_Network#Trophies" title="PlayStation Network">trophies</a>" on the PlayStation ports, and "achievements" in <i>Bedrock Edition</i> and the Xbox ports.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2024)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Gameplay is in the <a href="/wiki/First-person_(video_games)" title="First-person (video games)">first-person perspective</a> by default, but players have the option of a third-person perspective.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> The game world is composed of rough 3D objects—mainly cubes and fluids, and commonly called "blocks"—representing various materials, such as dirt, stone, ores, tree trunks (known as 'Logs'), water, and lava. The core gameplay revolves around picking up and placing these objects. These blocks are arranged in a 3D grid, while players can move freely around the world. Players can "mine" blocks and then place them elsewhere, enabling them to build things.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Many commentators have described the game's physics system as unrealistic.<sup id="cite_ref-Minecraft_In_Education_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Minecraft_In_Education-29">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> The game also contains a material called redstone, which can be used to make primitive mechanical devices, electrical circuits, and <a href="/wiki/Logic_gate" title="Logic gate">logic gates</a>, allowing for the construction of many complex systems.<sup id="cite_ref-RedstoneComputer_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RedstoneComputer-30">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Minecraft_explore_landscape.png" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="The default player skin, Steve, stands on a cliffside overlooking a village in a forest. In the distance, there is a small mountain range. The sun is setting to the right, making the sky turn pink and blue." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/17/Minecraft_explore_landscape.png/220px-Minecraft_explore_landscape.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="123" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/17/Minecraft_explore_landscape.png/330px-Minecraft_explore_landscape.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/1/17/Minecraft_explore_landscape.png 2x" data-file-width="421" data-file-height="236" /></a><figcaption>An example of <i>Minecraft</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> procedurally generated terrain, including a village and the default skin <a href="/wiki/Steve_(Minecraft)" title="Steve (Minecraft)">Steve</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>The game world is virtually infinite<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;i&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Procedural_generation" title="Procedural generation">procedurally generated</a> as players explore it, using a <a href="/wiki/Map_seed" title="Map seed">map seed</a> that is obtained from the <a href="/wiki/System_time" title="System time">system clock</a> at the time of world creation (or manually specified by the player).<sup id="cite_ref-NotchExplain1_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NotchExplain1-33">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NotchExplain2_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NotchExplain2-34">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Beginner&#39;s_guide_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beginner&#39;s_guide-35">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> There are limits on vertical movement, but <i>Minecraft</i> allows an infinitely large game world to be generated on the horizontal plane. Due to technical issues when extremely distant locations are reached, however, there is a barrier preventing players from traversing to locations beyond 30 million blocks from the center.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;j&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:AGE_MATTERS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:AGE MATTERS"><span title="Source is from 2011. The game quite likely works different now at a technical level than it did back then. (October 2022)">obsolete&#160;source</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The game achieves this by splitting the world data into smaller 16 by 16 sections called "chunks" that are only created or loaded when players are nearby.<sup id="cite_ref-NotchExplain1_33-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NotchExplain1-33">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The world is divided into <a href="/wiki/Biome" title="Biome">biomes</a> ranging from deserts to jungles to snowfields;<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> the terrain includes plains, mountains, forests, caves, and bodies of water or lava.<sup id="cite_ref-Beginner&#39;s_guide_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beginner&#39;s_guide-35">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> The in-game <a href="/wiki/Timekeeping_in_games" title="Timekeeping in games">time system</a> follows a day and night cycle, with one full cycle lasting for 20 real-time minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Minecraft_Mobs.png" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="Standing on a flat grassy plain against a blue sky, there is a green zombie wearing a blue shirt and purple pants; a large spider with red eyes; a tall, black, slender creature with purple eyes; a green, four-legged creature; and a skeleton." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c9/Minecraft_Mobs.png/220px-Minecraft_Mobs.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="128" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c9/Minecraft_Mobs.png/330px-Minecraft_Mobs.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/c/c9/Minecraft_Mobs.png 2x" data-file-width="417" data-file-height="242" /></a><figcaption>Some of <i>Minecraft</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> monsters, displayed from left to right: a zombie, a spider, an enderman, a <a href="/wiki/Creeper_(Minecraft)" title="Creeper (Minecraft)">creeper</a>, and a skeleton. All are from the Overworld.</figcaption></figure>
<p>When starting a new world, players must choose one of five game modes, as well as one of four difficulties, ranging from "Peaceful" to "Hard". Increasing the difficulty of the game causes the player to take more <a href="/wiki/Health_(game_terminology)" title="Health (game terminology)">damage</a> from <a href="/wiki/Mob_(video_games)" title="Mob (video games)">mobs</a> (non-player characters), as well as having other difficulty-specific effects. For example, the Peaceful difficulty prevents hostile mobs from <a href="/wiki/Spawning_(video_games)" title="Spawning (video games)">spawning</a>, and the Hard difficulty allows players to starve to death if their hunger bar is depleted.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2024)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Once selected, the difficulty can be changed, but the game mode is locked and can only be changed with <a href="/wiki/Cheating_in_video_games" title="Cheating in video games">cheats</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2024)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>New players are given a randomly selected default character <a href="/wiki/Skin_(computing)" class="mw-redirect" title="Skin (computing)">skin</a> out of 9 possibilities, including <a href="/wiki/Steve_(Minecraft)" title="Steve (Minecraft)">Steve</a> or Alex,<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> but the option to create custom skins was made available in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Players encounter various mobs, such as animals, villagers, and hostile creatures.<sup id="cite_ref-Update_May_2012_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Update_May_2012-43">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Passive mobs, such as cows, pigs, and chickens, can be hunted for food and crafting materials. They spawn in the daytime, while hostile mobs—including large spiders, witches, creepers, skeletons, endermen, and zombies—spawn during nighttime or in dark places such as caves.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2024)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Some hostile mobs, such as zombies, skeletons and drowned (underwater versions of zombies), burn under the sun if they have no headgear.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2024)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Other creatures unique to <i>Minecraft</i> include the <a href="/wiki/Creeper_(Minecraft)" title="Creeper (Minecraft)">creeper</a> (an exploding creature that sneaks up on the player) and the enderman (a creature with the ability to <a href="/wiki/Teleportation" title="Teleportation">teleport</a> as well as pick up and place blocks).<sup id="cite_ref-Eurogamer_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eurogamer-45">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> There are also variants of mobs that spawn in different conditions; for example, zombies have husk and drowned variants that spawn in deserts and oceans, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dimensions">Dimensions</span></h3>
<p><i>Minecraft</i> has two alternative dimensions besides the Overworld (the main world): the Nether and the End.<sup id="cite_ref-Eurogamer_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eurogamer-45">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Nether">The Nether</span></h4>
<p>The Nether is a <a href="/wiki/Hell" title="Hell">hell</a>-like underworld dimension accessed via either a player-built obsidian portal or one of the Ruined Portals randomly generated throughout the world. It contains many unique resources and can be used to travel great distances in the Overworld, due to every block traveled in the Nether being equivalent to 8 blocks traveled in the Overworld.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> Water cannot exist in the Nether, as it vaporizes instantly.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> The Nether is mainly populated by pigman-like mobs called piglins and their zombified counterparts, plus floating balloon-like mobs called ghasts.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> The piglins are considered particularly noteworthy because of their <a href="/wiki/Bartering" class="mw-redirect" title="Bartering">bartering</a> system, where the player can give them gold ingots and receive items in return.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> The player can also build an optional <a href="/wiki/Boss_(video_games)" title="Boss (video games)">boss</a> mob called The Wither out of materials found in the Nether.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_End">The End</span></h4>
<p>The End is reached by underground portals in the Overworld. It consists of islands floating above a dark, bottomless void. A <a href="/wiki/Boss_enemy_(video_games)" class="mw-redirect" title="Boss enemy (video games)">boss enemy</a> called the Ender Dragon guards the largest, central island.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Killing the dragon opens access to an exit portal, which, when entered, cues the game's ending credits and the <a href="/wiki/End_Poem" title="End Poem">End Poem</a>, a roughly 1,500-word work written by Irish novelist <a href="/wiki/Julian_Gough" title="Julian Gough">Julian Gough</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-parker_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-parker-53">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> which takes about nine minutes to scroll past<sup id="cite_ref-litchfield_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-litchfield-54">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> and is the game's only narrative text<sup id="cite_ref-moloney_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-moloney-55">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> and only text of significant length directed at the player.<sup id="cite_ref-anthony_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-anthony-56">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Pages: 10–12">&#58;&#8202;10–12&#8202;</span></sup> At the conclusion of the credits, the player is teleported back to their respawn point and may continue the game indefinitely.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Game_modes">Game modes</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Survival_mode">Survival mode</span></h4>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Minecraft_-_Crafting_a_stone_axe_screenshot.png" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="The player attempting to make a stone axe by placing the required materials into the crafting grid, a 3x3 block of item spaces hovering over the standard inventory, which is filled with other items." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b1/Minecraft_-_Crafting_a_stone_axe_screenshot.png/220px-Minecraft_-_Crafting_a_stone_axe_screenshot.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="128" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b1/Minecraft_-_Crafting_a_stone_axe_screenshot.png/330px-Minecraft_-_Crafting_a_stone_axe_screenshot.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/b/b1/Minecraft_-_Crafting_a_stone_axe_screenshot.png 2x" data-file-width="417" data-file-height="242" /></a><figcaption>The crafting menu in <i>Minecraft</i>, showing the crafting recipe of a stone axe as well as some other blocks and items in the player's inventory</figcaption></figure>
<p>In survival mode, players have to gather natural resources such as wood and stone found in the environment in order to craft certain blocks and items.<sup id="cite_ref-Beginner&#39;s_guide_35-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beginner&#39;s_guide-35">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Depending on the difficulty, monsters spawn in darker areas outside a certain radius of the character, requiring players to build a shelter at night.<sup id="cite_ref-Beginner&#39;s_guide_35-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beginner&#39;s_guide-35">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> The mode also has a <a href="/wiki/Health_(game_terminology)" title="Health (game terminology)">health bar</a> which is depleted by attacks from mobs, falls, drowning, falling into lava, suffocation, starvation, and other events.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2024)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Players also have a hunger bar, which must be periodically refilled by eating food in-game (except in peaceful difficulty).<sup id="cite_ref-:8_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:8-58">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> If the hunger bar is depleted, automatic healing will stop and eventually health will deplete. Health replenishes when players have a nearly full hunger bar or continuously on peaceful difficulty.<sup id="cite_ref-:8_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:8-58">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Players can craft a wide variety of items in <i>Minecraft</i>. Craftable items include armor, which mitigates damage from attacks; weapons (such as swords or axes), which allows monsters and animals to be killed more easily; and tools (such as pickaxes or hoes), which break certain types of blocks more quickly. Some items have multiple tiers depending on the material used to craft them, with higher-tier items being more effective and durable. Players can construct furnaces, which can cook food, process ores, and convert materials into other materials.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Players may also exchange goods with a villager (<a href="/wiki/Non-player_character" title="Non-player character">NPC</a>) through a trading system, which involves trading emeralds for different goods and vice versa.<sup id="cite_ref-Trading_update_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trading_update-60">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Update_May_2012_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Update_May_2012-43">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The game has an inventory system, allowing players to carry a limited number of items.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Upon dying, items in the players' inventories are dropped unless the game is reconfigured not to do so. Players then re-spawn at their spawn point, which by default is where players first spawn in the game and can be reset by sleeping in a bed (in the overworld)<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> or using a respawn anchor (in the Nether).<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Dropped items can be recovered if players can reach them before they disappear or despawn after 5 minutes. Players may acquire <a href="/wiki/Experience_point" title="Experience point">experience points</a> by killing mobs and other players, mining, smelting ores, <a href="/wiki/Animal_breeding" title="Animal breeding">breeding animals</a>, and cooking food. Experience can then be spent on <a href="/wiki/Incantation" title="Incantation">enchanting</a> tools, armor and weapons.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2024)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Enchanted items are generally more powerful, last longer, or have other special effects.<sup id="cite_ref-Controls_and_Settings_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Controls_and_Settings-64">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Creative_mode">Creative mode</span></h4>
<p>In creative mode, players have access to nearly all resources and items in the game through the inventory menu and can place or remove them instantly.<sup id="cite_ref-Creative_Mode_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Creative_Mode-65">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Players can toggle the ability to fly freely around the game world at will, and their characters do not take any damage and are not affected by hunger.<sup id="cite_ref-Creative_Mode_2_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Creative_Mode_2-66">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> The game mode helps players focus on building and creating projects of any size without disturbance.<sup id="cite_ref-Creative_Mode_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Creative_Mode-65">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_game_modes">Other game modes</span></h4>
<p><i>Minecraft</i> includes other game modes such as spectator mode, which allows players to fly through blocks. Hardcore mode, available only in <i>Java Edition</i>, is a survival mode variant in which, upon death, the player may only view the world in spectator mode or return to the game's menu.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Adventure mode is a survival mode variant with possible restrictions added by a creator of a map.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RPS_–_1.3aug_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RPS_–_1.3aug-71">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Multiplayer">Multiplayer</span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Minecraft_server" title="Minecraft server"><i>Minecraft</i> server</a></div>
<p>Multiplayer in <i>Minecraft</i> enables multiple players to interact and communicate with each other on a single world. It is available through direct game-to-game multiplayer, LAN play, local split screen (console-only), and servers (player-hosted and business-hosted).<sup id="cite_ref-Multiplayer_servers_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Multiplayer_servers-72">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> Players can run their own servers, use a hosting provider, or connect directly to another player's game via Xbox Live. Single-player worlds have <a href="/wiki/Local_area_network" title="Local area network">local area network</a> support, allowing players to join a world on locally interconnected computers without a server setup.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> <i>Minecraft</i> multiplayer servers are guided by server operators, who have access to server commands such as setting the time of day and teleporting players. Operators can also set up restrictions concerning which usernames or <a href="/wiki/IP_address" title="IP address">IP addresses</a> are allowed or disallowed to enter the server.<sup id="cite_ref-Multiplayer_servers_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Multiplayer_servers-72">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> Multiplayer servers have a wide range of activities, with some servers having their own unique rules and customs. The largest and most popular server is <a href="/wiki/Hypixel" title="Hypixel">Hypixel</a>, which has been visited by over 14 million unique players.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-riotgames_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-riotgames-75">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Player_versus_player" title="Player versus player">Player versus player</a> combat (PvP) can be enabled to allow fighting between players.<sup id="cite_ref-pcgamer_minecraft_future_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pcgamer_minecraft_future-76">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> Many servers have custom plugins that allow actions that are not normally possible.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Minecraft_Realms"><i>Minecraft Realms</i></span></h4>
<p>In 2013, Mojang announced <i>Minecraft Realms</i>, a server hosting service intended to enable players to run server multiplayer games easily and safely without having to set up their own.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pcgamesn_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pcgamesn-78">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Unlike a standard server, only invited players can join Realms servers, and these servers do not use IP addresses. <i>Minecraft: Java Edition</i> Realms server owners can invite up to twenty people to play on their server, with up to ten players online at a time. <i>Minecraft</i> Realms server owners can invite up to 3,000 people to play on their server, with up to ten players online at one time.<sup id="cite_ref-Minecraft_Realms_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Minecraft_Realms-79">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> The <i>Minecraft: Java Edition</i> Realms servers do not support user-made plugins, but players can play custom <i>Minecraft</i> maps.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> <i>Minecraft</i> Realms servers support user-made add-ons, resource packs, behavior packs, and custom <i>Minecraft</i> maps.<sup id="cite_ref-Minecraft_Realms_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Minecraft_Realms-79">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> At <a href="/wiki/E3_2016" title="E3 2016">Electronic Entertainment Expo 2016</a>, support for <a href="/wiki/Cross-platform_play" title="Cross-platform play">cross-platform play</a> between <a href="/wiki/Windows_10" title="Windows 10">Windows 10</a>, <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">iOS</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a> platforms was added through Realms starting in June 2016,<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> with <a href="/wiki/Xbox_One" title="Xbox One">Xbox One</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nintendo_Switch" title="Nintendo Switch">Nintendo Switch</a> support to come later in 2017,<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> and support for <a href="/wiki/Virtual_reality" title="Virtual reality">virtual reality</a> devices. On 31 July 2017, Mojang released the beta version of the update allowing cross-platform play.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> Nintendo Switch support for Realms was released in July 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Customization">Customization</span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Minecraft_modding" title="Minecraft modding"><i>Minecraft</i> modding</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Tinkers_Construct_smeltery.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Tinkers_Construct_smeltery.png/220px-Tinkers_Construct_smeltery.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="151" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Tinkers_Construct_smeltery.png/330px-Tinkers_Construct_smeltery.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Tinkers_Construct_smeltery.png/440px-Tinkers_Construct_smeltery.png 2x" data-file-width="907" data-file-height="621" /></a><figcaption>A smeltery within the mod <i>Tinkers' Construct</i></figcaption></figure>
<p>The <i>modding community</i> consists of fans, users and third-party programmers. Using a variety of <a href="/wiki/API" title="API">application program interfaces</a> that have arisen over time, they have produced a wide variety of <a href="/wiki/Downloadable_content" title="Downloadable content">downloadable content</a> for <i>Minecraft</i>, such as modifications, texture packs and custom maps. Modifications of the <i>Minecraft</i> code, called <i><a href="/wiki/Video_game_modding" title="Video game modding">mods</a></i>, add a variety of gameplay changes, ranging from new blocks, items, and mobs to entire arrays of mechanisms.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> The modding community is responsible for a substantial supply of mods from ones that enhance gameplay, such as <a href="/wiki/Mini-map" title="Mini-map">mini-maps</a>, waypoints, and durability counters, to ones that add to the game elements from other video games and media.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2024)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> While a variety of mod frameworks were independently developed by <a href="/wiki/Reverse_engineering" title="Reverse engineering">reverse engineering</a> the code, Mojang has also enhanced <a href="/wiki/Vanilla_software" title="Vanilla software">vanilla</a> <i>Minecraft</i> with official frameworks for modification, allowing the production of community-created resource packs, which alter certain game elements including textures and sounds.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> Players can also create their own "maps" (custom world save files) which often contain specific rules, challenges, puzzles and quests, and share them for others to play.<sup id="cite_ref-Custom_maps_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Custom_maps-88">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> Mojang added an adventure mode in August 2012<sup id="cite_ref-RPS_–_1.3july_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RPS_–_1.3july-89">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> and "command blocks" in October 2012,<sup id="cite_ref-Gallegos_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gallegos-90">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> which were created specially for custom maps in <i>Java Edition</i>. Data packs, introduced in version 1.13 of the <i>Java Edition</i>, allow further customization, including the ability to add new advancements, dimensions, functions, loot tables, predicates, recipes, structures, tags, world generation settings, and biomes‌.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <i>Xbox 360 Edition</i> supported downloadable content, which was available to purchase via the <a href="/wiki/Xbox_Games_Store" title="Xbox Games Store">Xbox Games Store</a>; these content packs usually contained additional character skins.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> It later received support for texture packs in its twelfth title update while introducing "mash-up packs", which combined texture packs with skin packs and changes to the game's sounds, music and user interface.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> The first mash-up pack (and by extension, the first texture pack) for the <i>Xbox 360 Edition</i> was released on 4 September 2013, and was themed after the <i><a href="/wiki/Mass_Effect" title="Mass Effect">Mass Effect</a></i> franchise.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> Unlike <i>Java Edition</i>, however, the <i>Xbox 360 Edition</i> did not support player-made mods or custom maps.<sup id="cite_ref-IGN_Xbox_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IGN_Xbox-96">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> A cross-promotional resource pack based on the <i><a href="/wiki/Super_Mario" title="Super Mario">Super Mario</a></i> franchise by Nintendo was released for the <i>Wii U Edition</i> worldwide on 17 May 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> A mash-up pack based on <i>Fallout</i> was announced for release on the <i>Wii U Edition</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> In April 2018, <a href="/wiki/Malware" title="Malware">malware</a> was discovered in several downloadable user-made <i>Minecraft</i> skins for use with the <i>Java Edition</i> of the game.<sup id="cite_ref-pcgamermalware_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pcgamermalware-99">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-varietymalware1_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-varietymalware1-100">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Avast" title="Avast">Avast</a> stated that nearly 50,000 accounts were infected, and when activated, the malware would attempt to <a href="/wiki/Disk_formatting#Reformatting" title="Disk formatting">reformat</a> the user's hard drive.<sup id="cite_ref-varietymalware1_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-varietymalware1-100">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pcgamermalware_99-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pcgamermalware-99">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> Mojang promptly patched the issue, and released a statement stating that "the code would not be run or read by the game itself",<sup id="cite_ref-pcgamermalware_99-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pcgamermalware-99">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> and would only run when the image containing the skin itself was opened.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2017, Mojang released an update known as the "Discovery Update" to the <i>Bedrock</i> version of the game.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> The update includes a new map, a new game mode, the "Marketplace", a catalogue of user-generated content that gives <i>Minecraft</i> creators "another way to make a living from the game", and more.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Development">Development</span></h2>
<figure class="mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Notch_receives_the_Pioneer_Award_at_GDC_2016_(cropped).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Notch_receives_the_Pioneer_Award_at_GDC_2016_%28cropped%29.jpg/180px-Notch_receives_the_Pioneer_Award_at_GDC_2016_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="205" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Notch_receives_the_Pioneer_Award_at_GDC_2016_%28cropped%29.jpg/270px-Notch_receives_the_Pioneer_Award_at_GDC_2016_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Notch_receives_the_Pioneer_Award_at_GDC_2016_%28cropped%29.jpg/360px-Notch_receives_the_Pioneer_Award_at_GDC_2016_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1514" data-file-height="1724" /></a><figcaption><i>Minecraft</i> creator <a href="/wiki/Markus_Persson" title="Markus Persson">Markus "Notch" Persson</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Game_Developers_Conference" title="Game Developers Conference">GDC</a> in 2016</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Jens_Bergensten_Minecon.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Jens_Bergensten_Minecon.jpg/180px-Jens_Bergensten_Minecon.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="180" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Jens_Bergensten_Minecon.jpg/270px-Jens_Bergensten_Minecon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Jens_Bergensten_Minecon.jpg/360px-Jens_Bergensten_Minecon.jpg 2x" data-file-width="592" data-file-height="592" /></a><figcaption><i>Minecraft</i> lead designer and creative director <a href="/wiki/Jens_Bergensten" title="Jens Bergensten">Jens "Jeb_" Bergensten</a> in 2011</figcaption></figure>
