<p>Before coming up with <i>Minecraft</i>, <a href="/wiki/Markus_Persson" title="Markus Persson">Markus "Notch" Persson</a> was a game developer with <a href="/wiki/King_(company)" title="King (company)">King</a> through March 2009, at the time serving mostly <a href="/wiki/Browser_game" title="Browser game">browser games</a>, during which he learnt a number of different programming languages.<sup id="cite_ref-wired_origins_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wired_origins-106">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> He would prototype his own games during his off-hours at home, often based on inspiration he found from other games, and participated frequently on the <a href="/wiki/TIGSource" title="TIGSource">TIGSource</a> forums for independent developers.<sup id="cite_ref-wired_origins_106-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wired_origins-106">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> One of these personal projects was called "RubyDung", a base-building game inspired by <i><a href="/wiki/Dwarf_Fortress" title="Dwarf Fortress">Dwarf Fortress</a></i>, but as an isometric three dimensional game like <i><a href="/wiki/RollerCoaster_Tycoon" title="RollerCoaster Tycoon">RollerCoaster Tycoon</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-TechRadar:_History_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TechRadar:_History-107">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> He had already made a 3D texture mapper for another zombie game prototype he had started to try to emulate the style of <i><a href="/wiki/Grand_Theft_Auto:_Chinatown_Wars" title="Grand Theft Auto: Chinatown Wars">Grand Theft Auto: Chinatown Wars</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-rubydung_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rubydung-108">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> Among the features in "RubyDung" he explored was a first-person view similar to <i><a href="/wiki/Dungeon_Keeper" title="Dungeon Keeper">Dungeon Keeper</a></i> but at the time, felt the graphics were too pixelated and omitted this mode.<sup id="cite_ref-rubydung_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rubydung-108">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GSint_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GSint-109">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> Around March 2009, Persson left King and joined <a href="/wiki/JAlbum" title="JAlbum">jAlbum</a>, but otherwise kept working on his prototypes.<sup id="cite_ref-Story_of_Mojang_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Story_of_Mojang-110">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GSint_109-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GSint-109">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GAMASUTRA_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GAMASUTRA-111">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/Zachtronics" title="Zachtronics">Infiniminer</a></i>, a block-based open-ended mining game first released in April 2009, sparked Persson's inspiration for how to take "RubyDung" forward.<sup id="cite_ref-rubydung_108-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rubydung-108">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> <i>Infiniminer</i> heavily influenced the visual style of gameplay, including bringing back the first-person mode, the "blocky" visual style and the block-building fundamentals.<sup id="cite_ref-rubydung_108-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rubydung-108">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> However, unlike <i>Infiniminer</i>, Persson wanted <i>Minecraft</i> to have <a href="/wiki/Role-playing_game" title="Role-playing game">RPG</a> elements.<sup id="cite_ref-Blockbuster_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Blockbuster-112">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The original edition of <i>Minecraft</i>, now known as the <i>Java Edition</i>, was first developed in May 2009. Persson released a test video on YouTube of an early version of <i>Minecraft</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-rubydung_108-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rubydung-108">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> The base program of <i>Minecraft</i> was completed by Persson over a weekend in that month and a private testing was released on TigIRC on 16 May 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> The game was first released to the public on 17 May 2009 as a developmental release on <i>TIGSource</i> forums.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> Persson updated the game based on feedback from the forums.<sup id="cite_ref-wired_origins_106-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wired_origins-106">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> This version later became known as the <i>Classic</i> version.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> Further developmental phases dubbed as <i>Survival Test</i>, <i>Indev,</i> and <i>Infdev</i> were released in 2009 and 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-GSint_109-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GSint-109">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The first major update, dubbed <a href="/wiki/Video_game_development" title="Video game development">Alpha</a>, was released on 30 June 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> Although Persson maintained a day job with Jalbum.net at first, he later quit in order to work on <i>Minecraft</i> full-time as sales of the alpha version of the game expanded.<sup id="cite_ref-PCGAMERinterview_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PCGAMERinterview-120">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> Persson continued to update the game with releases distributed to users automatically. These updates included new items, new blocks, new mobs, survival mode, and changes to the game's behavior (e.g. how water flows).<sup id="cite_ref-PCGAMERinterview_120-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PCGAMERinterview-120">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> To back the development of <i>Minecraft</i>, Persson set up a video game company, Mojang, with the money earned from the game.<sup id="cite_ref-Cult_and_merchandise_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cult_and_merchandise-121">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-LackOfUpdates_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LackOfUpdates-122">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MCcompany_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MCcompany-123">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> Mojang co-founders included Jakob Porser, one of Persson's coworkers from King, and Carl Manneh, jAlbum's CEO.<sup id="cite_ref-wired_origins_106-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wired_origins-106">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 11 December 2010, Persson announced that <i>Minecraft</i> was entering its beta testing phase on 20 December 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> He further stated that bug fixes and all updates leading up to and including the release would still be free.<sup id="cite_ref-BetaDate_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BetaDate-125">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> Over the course of the development, Mojang hired several new employees to work on the project.<sup id="cite_ref-MCMannehMollstam_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MCMannehMollstam-126">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Mojang moved the game out of beta and released the full version on 18 November 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-PC_release_date_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PC_release_date-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> On 1 December 2011, <a href="/wiki/Jens_Bergensten" title="Jens Bergensten">Jens "Jeb" Bergensten</a> took full creative control over <i>Minecraft</i>, replacing Persson as lead designer.<sup id="cite_ref-bergleaddev_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bergleaddev-127">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> On 28 February 2012, Mojang announced that they had hired the developers of the popular "Bukkit" developer API for <i>Minecraft</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-pcgamer_minecraft_future_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pcgamer_minecraft_future-76">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> to improve <i>Minecraft</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> support of <a href="/wiki/Minecraft_modding" title="Minecraft modding">server modifications</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> This acquisition also included Mojang apparently taking full ownership of the CraftBukkit server mod which enables the use of Bukkit,<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> although the validity of this claim was questioned due to its status as an <a href="/wiki/Open-source_software" title="Open-source software">open-source</a> project with many contributors, licensed under the <a href="/wiki/GNU_General_Public_License" title="GNU General Public License">GNU General Public License</a> and <a href="/wiki/GNU_Lesser_General_Public_License" title="GNU Lesser General Public License">Lesser General Public License</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-gon-craftbukkitdmca_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gon-craftbukkitdmca-130">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 15 September 2014, <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a> announced a $2.5 billion deal to buy Mojang, along with the ownership of the <i>Minecraft</i> intellectual property.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-131">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:3_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-132">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:4_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-133">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> The deal was suggested by Persson when he posted a tweet asking a corporation to buy his share of the game after receiving criticism for enforcing terms in the game's <a href="/wiki/End-user_license_agreement" title="End-user license agreement">end-user license agreement</a> (EULA), which had been present in the EULA in the prior three years.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MicrosoftMinecraft4_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MicrosoftMinecraft4-136">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> According to Persson, Mojang CEO Carl Manneh received a call from a Microsoft executive shortly after the tweet, asking if Persson was serious about a deal. Mojang was also approached by other companies including <a href="/wiki/Activision_Blizzard" title="Activision Blizzard">Activision Blizzard</a> and <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Arts" title="Electronic Arts">Electronic Arts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MicrosoftMinecraft4_136-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MicrosoftMinecraft4-136">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> The deal with Microsoft was arbitrated on 6 November 2014 and led to Persson becoming one of <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span> "World's Billionaires".<sup id="cite_ref-MicrosoftMinecraft1_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MicrosoftMinecraft1-137">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MicrosoftMinecraft2_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MicrosoftMinecraft2-138">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MicrosoftMinecraft3_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MicrosoftMinecraft3-139">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MicrosoftMinecraft4_136-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MicrosoftMinecraft4-136">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since the first full release of <i>Minecraft</i>, dubbed the "Adventure Update", the game has been continuously updated with many major updates, available for free to users who have already purchased the game.<sup id="cite_ref-notchMigr_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-notchMigr-140">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> Early updates frequently introduced gameplay-altering mechanics while more recent updates tend to enhance the game through additional content or tweaks to existing features.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="The current source is insufficiently reliable (WP:NOTRS). (June 2022)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The most recent major update to the game was "Trails &amp; Tales", which released in June 2023 and added new creatures, biomes, and items.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The original version of the game was renamed to <i>Minecraft: Java Edition</i> on 18 September 2017 to separate it from <i>Bedrock Edition</i>, which was renamed to just <i>Minecraft</i> by the <i>Better Together Update</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-144">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <i>Bedrock Edition</i> has also been regularly updated, with these updates now matching the themes of <i>Java Edition</i> updates. Other versions of the game such as the various console editions and <i>Pocket Edition</i> were either merged into <i>Bedrock</i> or discontinued and as such have not received further updates.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_144-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-144">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 16 April 2020, a <a href="/wiki/Software_release_life_cycle#Beta" title="Software release life cycle">beta</a> version of <i>Minecraft</i> implementing <a href="/wiki/Physically_based_rendering" title="Physically based rendering">physically based rendering</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ray_tracing_(graphics)" title="Ray tracing (graphics)">ray tracing</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Deep_learning_super_sampling" title="Deep learning super sampling">DLSS</a> was released by <a href="/wiki/Nvidia" title="Nvidia">Nvidia</a> on <a href="/wiki/Nvidia_RTX" title="Nvidia RTX">RTX</a>-enabled <a href="/wiki/Graphics_processing_unit" title="Graphics processing unit">GPUs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> The final version was released on 8 December 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><span class="anchor" id="Pocket_Edition"></span><span class="anchor" id="MC:PE"></span><span class="anchor" id="MCPE"></span>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Minecraft:_Pocket_Edition"><i>Minecraft: Pocket Edition</i></span></h3>
<p>In August 2011, <i>Minecraft: Pocket Edition</i> was released for the <a href="/wiki/Xperia_Play" title="Xperia Play">Xperia Play</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Google_Play" title="Google Play">Android Market</a> as an early alpha version. It was then released for several other compatible devices on 8 October 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-MobileGamas_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MobileGamas-147">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MobileKotaku_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MobileKotaku-148">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> An <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">iOS</a> version of <i>Minecraft</i> was released on 17 November 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> A port was made available for <a href="/wiki/Windows_Phone" title="Windows Phone">Windows Phones</a> shortly after Microsoft acquired Mojang.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> The port concentrates on the creative building and the primitive survival aspect of the game and did not contain all the features of the PC release.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2023)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> On his Twitter account, Jens Bergensten said that the <i>Pocket Edition</i> of <i>Minecraft</i> is written in C++ and not Java, due to iOS not being able to support Java.<sup id="cite_ref-PE_C++_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PE_C++-151">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> However, there now exists a way to play <i>Java Edition</i> on both Android and iOS devices.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 10 December 2014, a port of <i>Pocket Edition</i> was released for <a href="/wiki/Windows_Phone_8.1" title="Windows Phone 8.1">Windows Phone 8.1</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-engadget-wpmc_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-engadget-wpmc-154">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> In January 2017, Microsoft announced that it would no longer maintain the Windows Phone versions of <i>Pocket Edition</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-ars-mcw10discontinued_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ars-mcw10discontinued-155">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> On 19 December 2016, the full version of <i>Minecraft: Pocket Edition</i> was released on iOS, Android, and Windows Phone.
</p><p><i>Pocket Edition</i> was remade into the <i>Bedrock Edition</i> in 2017, enabling <a href="/wiki/Cross-platform_play" title="Cross-platform play">cross-platform play</a> with the <i>Xbox One</i> and <i>Nintendo Switch Editions</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-:12_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:12-156">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><span class="anchor" id="Minecraft:_Xbox_360_Edition"></span><span class="anchor" id="Xbox_360_Edition"></span><span class="anchor" id="Xbox_360"></span><span class="anchor" id="360"></span><span class="anchor" id="Minecraft:_Xbox_One_Edition"></span><span class="anchor" id="Xbox_One_Edition"></span><span class="anchor" id="Xbox_One"></span><span class="anchor" id="Minecraft:_PlayStation_3_Edition"></span><span class="anchor" id="Minecraft:_PS3_Edition"></span><span class="anchor" id="PS3_Edition"></span><span class="anchor" id="PS3"></span><span class="anchor" id="Minecraft:_PlayStaion_4_Edition"></span><span class="anchor" id="Minecraft:_PS4_Edition"></span><span class="anchor" id="PS4"></span><span class="anchor" id="Minecraft:_PlayStation_Vita_Edition"></span><span class="anchor" id="Minecraft:_PSV_Edition"></span><span class="anchor" id="PSV"></span><span class="anchor" id="Minecraft:_Wii_U_Edition"></span><span class="anchor" id="Wii_U_Edition"></span><span class="anchor" id="Wii_U"></span><span class="anchor" id="Minecraft:_Nintendo_Switch_Edition"></span><span class="anchor" id="Nintendo_Switch_Edition"></span><span class="anchor" id="Nintendo_Switch"></span><span class="anchor" id="Minecraft:_Nintendo_3DS_Edition"></span>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy_Console_Editions"><i>Legacy Console Editions</i></span></h3>
<p>An <a href="/wiki/Xbox_360" title="Xbox 360">Xbox 360</a> version of the game, developed by <a href="/wiki/4J_Studios" title="4J Studios">4J Studios</a>, was released on 9 May 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-xboxpress_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xboxpress-157">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-xboxreleasedate_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xboxreleasedate-158">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> On 22 March 2012, it was announced that <i>Minecraft</i> would be the flagship game in a new Xbox Live promotion called <i>Arcade NEXT</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-xboxreleasedate_158-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xboxreleasedate-158">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> The game differs from the home computer versions in a number of ways, including a newly designed crafting system, the control interface, in-game tutorials, split-screen multiplayer, and the ability to play with friends via <a href="/wiki/Xbox_network" title="Xbox network">Xbox Live</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GSpot_Xbox_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GSpot_Xbox-160">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> The worlds in the Xbox 360 version are also not "infinite", and are essentially barricaded by invisible walls.<sup id="cite_ref-GSpot_Xbox_160-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GSpot_Xbox-160">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> The Xbox 360 version was originally similar in content to older PC versions, but was gradually updated to bring it closer to the current PC version prior to its discontinuation.<sup id="cite_ref-xboxpress_157-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xboxpress-157">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> An Xbox One version featuring larger worlds among other enhancements<sup id="cite_ref-Microsoft_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Microsoft-163">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> was released on 5 September 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-Microsoft_163-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Microsoft-163">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Versions of the game for the <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_3" title="PlayStation 3">PlayStation 3</a> and <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_4" title="PlayStation 4">PlayStation 4</a> were released on 17 December 2013 and 4 September 2014 respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-PS4_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PS4-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The PlayStation 4 version was announced as a launch title, though it was eventually delayed.<sup id="cite_ref-ps4_launch_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ps4_launch-164">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gamespot1_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gamespot1-165">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> A version for <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_Vita" title="PlayStation Vita">PlayStation Vita</a> was also released in October 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-vita_launch_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vita_launch-166">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> Like the Xbox versions, the PlayStation versions were developed by 4J Studios.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 17 December 2015, <i>Minecraft: Wii U Edition</i> was released. The <a href="/wiki/Wii_U" title="Wii U">Wii U</a> version received a physical release on 17 June 2016 in North America,<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> in Japan on 23 June 2016,<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> and in Europe on 30 June 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Nintendo_Switch" title="Nintendo Switch">Nintendo Switch</a> version of the game was released on the <a href="/wiki/Nintendo_eShop" title="Nintendo eShop">Nintendo eShop</a> on 11 May 2017, along with a physical retail version set for a later date.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> During a <a href="/wiki/Nintendo_Direct" title="Nintendo Direct">Nintendo Direct</a> presentation on 13 September 2017, Nintendo announced that <i>Minecraft: New Nintendo 3DS Edition</i> would be available for download immediately after the livestream, and a physical copy available on a later date. The game is only compatible with the <a href="/wiki/New_Nintendo_3DS" title="New Nintendo 3DS">New 3DS and New 3DS XL</a> or <a href="/wiki/New_Nintendo_2DS_XL" class="mw-redirect" title="New Nintendo 2DS XL">New 2DS XL</a> systems and does not work with the original <a href="/wiki/Nintendo_3DS" title="Nintendo 3DS">3DS and 3DS XL</a> or <a href="/wiki/Nintendo_2DS" title="Nintendo 2DS">2DS</a> systems.<sup id="cite_ref-New3DS_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-New3DS-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 20 September 2017, the <i>Better Together Update</i> was released on the Xbox One, Windows 10, VR, and mobile versions of the game, which used the <i>Pocket Edition</i> engine to enable cross-platform play between each of these versions. This version of the game eventually became known as the <i>Bedrock Edition</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> Shortly after, the <i>Bedrock Edition</i> was also ported to the Nintendo Switch.
</p><p>On 18 December 2018, the PlayStation 3, PlayStation Vita, Xbox 360, and Wii U versions of <i>Minecraft</i> received their final update and would later become known as <i>Legacy Console Editions</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 15 January 2019, the New Nintendo 3DS version of <i>Minecraft</i> received its final update, effectively becoming discontinued as well.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The PlayStation 4 version of <i>Minecraft</i> was updated in December 2019 and became part of the <i>Bedrock Edition</i>, which enabled cross-platform play for users with a free Xbox Live account.<sup id="cite_ref-ps4_bedrock_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ps4_bedrock-175">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><span class="anchor" id="Education_Edition"></span>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Minecraft_Education"><i>Minecraft Education</i></span></h3>
<p><i>Minecraft Education</i> (known as <i>Minecraft: Education Edition</i> until December 2022)<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> is an educational version of the game, designed specifically for use in educational establishments such as schools, and built off of the <i>Bedrock Edition</i> codebase. It is available on <a href="/wiki/Windows_10" title="Windows 10">Windows 10</a>, <a href="/wiki/MacOS" title="MacOS">MacOS</a>, <a href="/wiki/IPadOS" title="IPadOS">iPadOS</a>, and <a href="/wiki/ChromeOS" title="ChromeOS">ChromeOS</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:22_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:22-178">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> It includes a Chemistry Resource Pack,<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> free lesson plans available online, and two free companion applications: Code Connection and Classroom Mode.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>An initial beta test was carried out between 9 June and 1 November 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> The full game was then released on Windows 10 and MacOS on 1 November 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> On 20 August 2018, Mojang announced that it would bring <i>Education Edition</i> to iPadOS in Autumn 2018. It was released to the App Store on 6 September 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> On 27 March 2019, it was announced that it would be operated by <a href="/wiki/JD.com" title="JD.com">JD.com</a> in China.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> On 26 June 2020, a public beta for the <i>Education Edition</i> was made available to <a href="/wiki/Google_Play" title="Google Play">Google Play</a> Store compatible Chromebooks. The full game was released to the Google Play Store for Chromebooks on 7 August 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-:22_178-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:22-178">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><span class="anchor" id="Minecraft:_China"></span>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Minecraft_China"><i>Minecraft China</i></span></h3>
<p>On 20 May 2016, <i>Minecraft China</i> was announced as a localized edition for China, where it was released under a licensing agreement between <a href="/wiki/NetEase" title="NetEase">NetEase</a> and Mojang.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> The PC edition was released for public testing on 8 August 2017. The iOS version was released on 15 September 2017, and the Android version was released on 12 October 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> The PC edition is based on the original <i>Java Edition</i>, while the iOS and Android mobile version is based on the <i>Bedrock Edition</i>. The edition is free-to-play and had over 300 million players by November 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-China-300m2_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-China-300m2-189">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><span class="anchor" id="Minecraft:_Windows_10_Edition"></span><span class="anchor" id="Windows_10_Edition"></span><span class="anchor" id="Windows_10"></span><span class="anchor" id="Minecraft_4K"></span>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_PC_versions">Other PC versions</span></h3>
<p>Apart from <i>Minecraft: Java Edition</i>, there are other versions of <i>Minecraft</i> for PC, including <i>Minecraft for Windows</i>, <i>Minecraft Classic</i>, <i>Minecraft 4K</i>, and a version for the <a href="/wiki/Raspberry_Pi" title="Raspberry Pi">Raspberry Pi</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Minecraft_for_Windows"><i>Minecraft for Windows</i></span></h4>
<p><i>Minecraft for Windows</i> is exclusive to Microsoft's Windows 10 and <a href="/wiki/Windows_11" title="Windows 11">Windows 11</a> operating systems. The <a href="/wiki/Video_game_development#Beta" title="Video game development">beta</a> release for Windows 10 launched on the <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Store" title="Microsoft Store">Windows Store</a> on 29 July 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After nearly one and a half years in beta, Microsoft fully released <i>Minecraft for Windows</i> on 19 December 2016. Called the "Ender Update", this release implemented new features to this version of <i>Minecraft</i> like world templates and add-on packs.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> This version has the ability to play with Xbox Live friends, and to play local multiplayer with owners of <i>Minecraft</i> on other <i>Bedrock</i> platforms. Other features include the ability to use multiple control schemes such as a gamepad, keyboard, or touchscreen (for <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Surface" title="Microsoft Surface">Microsoft Surface</a> and other touchscreen-enabled devices). Virtual reality support has been implemented, as well as the ability to record and take screenshots in-game via the Windows built-in GameDVR.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As of 7 June 2022, the <i>Java</i> and <i>Bedrock Editions</i> of <i>Minecraft</i> for Windows were merged into a single title for purchase; those who owned one version would automatically gain access to the other version. Both game versions would otherwise remain separate.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Minecraft_4K"><i>Minecraft 4K</i></span></h4>
<p><i>Minecraft 4K</i> is a simplified version of <i>Minecraft</i> similar to the Classic version that was developed for the <a href="/wiki/Java_4K_Game_Programming_Contest" title="Java 4K Game Programming Contest">Java 4K Game Programming Contest</a> "in way less than 4 kilobytes".<sup id="cite_ref-m4k_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-m4k-194">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> The map itself is finite—composed of 64×64×64 blocks—and the same world is generated every time. Players are restricted to placing or destroying blocks, which consist of grass, dirt, stone, wood, leaves, and brick.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Raspberry_Pi">Raspberry Pi</span></h4>
<p>A version of <i>Minecraft</i> for the Raspberry Pi was officially revealed at <a href="/wiki/Minecon" title="Minecon">Minecon</a> 2012. The <i>Pi Edition</i> is based on an alpha version of <i>Pocket Edition</i> with the added ability of using text commands to edit the game world. Players can open the game code and use the <a href="/wiki/Python_(programming_language)" title="Python (programming language)">Python</a> programming language to manipulate things in the game world.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> It also includes a scripting API to modify the game, and server software for multiplayer. The game was leaked on 20 December 2012, but was quickly pulled off.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> It was officially released on 11 February 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> Mojang stopped providing updates to <i>Minecraft: Raspberry Pi Edition</i> in 2016. It is preinstalled on <a href="/wiki/Raspberry_Pi_OS" title="Raspberry Pi OS">Raspberry Pi OS</a> and can be downloaded for free from the official <i>Minecraft</i> website.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_and_sound_design">Music and sound design</span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Minecraft" title="Music of Minecraft">Music of <i>Minecraft</i></a></div>
<p><i>Minecraft</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> music and sound effects were produced by German musician Daniel Rosenfeld, better known as <a href="/wiki/C418" title="C418">C418</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-credits_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-credits-200">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> To create the sound effects for the game, Rosenfeld made extensive use of <a href="/wiki/Foley_(filmmaking)" title="Foley (filmmaking)">foley</a> techniques. On learning the processes for the game, he remarked, "Foley’s an interesting thing, and I had to learn its subtleties. Early on, I wasn’t that knowledgeable about it. It’s a whole trial-and-error process. You just make a sound and eventually you go, “Oh my God, that’s it! Get the microphone!” There’s no set way of doing anything at all."<sup id="cite_ref-FACT2_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FACT2-201">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-redbull_202-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-redbull-202">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup>  He reminisced on creating the in-game sound for grass blocks, stating "It turns out that to make grass sounds you don’t actually walk on grass and record it, because grass sounds like nothing. What you want to do is get a VHS, break it apart, and just lightly touch the tape." According to Rosenfeld, his favorite sound to design for the game was the hisses of <a href="/wiki/Spiders" class="mw-redirect" title="Spiders">spiders</a>. He elaborates, "I like the spiders. Recording that was a whole day of me researching what a spider sounds like. Turns out, there are spiders that make little screeching sounds, so I think I got this recording of a fire hose, put it in a sampler, and just pitched it around until it sounded like a weird spider was talking to you."<sup id="cite_ref-FACT2_201-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FACT2-201">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Many sounds for the game were created accidentally or spontaneously. On the creation for the sound for the creeper, Rosenfeld recalled, "That was just a complete accident by Markus and me &#32;&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Sic" title="Sic">sic</a></i>&#93;. We just put in a placeholder sound of burning a matchstick. It seemed to work hilariously well, so we kept it."<sup id="cite_ref-TheGuardian_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TheGuardian-203">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> On other sounds, such as those of the zombie, Rosenfeld remarked, "I actually never wanted the zombies so scary. I intentionally made them sound comical. It’s nice to hear that they work so well [...]."<sup id="cite_ref-TheGuardian_203-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TheGuardian-203">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> Rosenfeld remarked that the sound engine was "terrible" to work with, remembering "If you had two song files at once, it [the game engine] would actually crash. There were so many more weird glitches like that the guys never really fixed because they were too busy with the actual game and not the sound engine."<sup id="cite_ref-redbull_202-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-redbull-202">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Background_music" title="Background music">background music</a> in <i>Minecraft</i> is instrumental <a href="/wiki/Ambient_music" title="Ambient music">ambient music</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> To compose the music of <i>Minecraft</i>, Rosenfeld used the package from <a href="/wiki/Ableton_Live" title="Ableton Live">Ableton Live</a>, along with several additional plug-ins. Speaking on them, Rosenfeld said "They can be pretty much everything from an effect to an entire orchestra. Additionally, I’ve got some synthesizers that are attached to the computer. Like a <a href="/wiki/Moog_Music" title="Moog Music">Moog Voyager</a>, Dave Smith Prophet 08 and a Virus TI."<sup id="cite_ref-TheGuardian_203-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TheGuardian-203">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> On 4 March 2011, Rosenfeld released a <a href="/wiki/Video_game_music" title="Video game music">soundtrack</a> titled <i><a href="/wiki/Minecraft_%E2%80%93_Volume_Alpha" title="Minecraft – Volume Alpha">Minecraft – Volume Alpha</a></i>; it includes most of the tracks featured in <i>Minecraft</i>, as well as other music not featured in the game.<sup id="cite_ref-Bandcamp_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bandcamp-205">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> Kirk Hamilton of <i><a href="/wiki/Kotaku" title="Kotaku">Kotaku</a></i> chose the music in <i>Minecraft</i> as one of the best video game soundtracks of 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> On 9 November 2013, Rosenfeld released the second official soundtrack, titled <i><a href="/wiki/Minecraft_%E2%80%93_Volume_Beta" title="Minecraft – Volume Beta">Minecraft – Volume Beta</a></i>, which includes the music that was added in later versions of the game.<sup id="cite_ref-Bandcamp2_207-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bandcamp2-207">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-208">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> A physical release of <i>Volume Alpha</i>, consisting of CDs, black vinyl, and limited-edition transparent green vinyl LPs, was issued by indie electronic label <a href="/wiki/Ghostly_International" title="Ghostly International">Ghostly International</a> on 21 August 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> On 14 August 2020, Ghostly released <i>Volume Beta</i> on CD and vinyl, with alternate color LPs and lenticular cover pressings released in limited quantities.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Rosenfeld's music remained the only music in the game until in 2020, "The Nether Update" had a new composer, <a href="/wiki/Lena_Raine" title="Lena Raine">Lena Raine</a>. Since then, other composers have made contributions, with Raine remaining as the new primary composer, such as in 1.18 "Caves &amp; Cliffs" soundtrack, along with <a href="/wiki/Kumi_Tanioka" title="Kumi Tanioka">Kumi Tanioka</a>, 1.19 "The Wild Update" soundtrack with Samuel Åberg, and 1.20 "Trails and Tales" Soundtrack, with the addition of Aaron Cherof's music. Ownership of all music besides Rosenfeld's independently released albums has been retained by Microsoft, with their label publishing all of the other artists' releases. <a href="/wiki/Gareth_Coker" title="Gareth Coker">Gareth Coker</a> also composed some of the music for the game's mini games from the Legacy Console editions.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-116release_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116release-215">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Rosenfeld had stated his intent to create a third album of music for the game in a 2015 interview with <i>FACT Magazine</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-FACT2_201-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FACT2-201">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> and confirmed its existence in a 2017 <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">tweet</a>, stating that his work on the record as of then had tallied up to be longer than the previous two albums combined, which in total clocks in at over 3 hours and 18 minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-TwitterConfirmMusic_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TwitterConfirmMusic-217">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> However, due to licensing issues with Microsoft, the third volume has since not seen release. On 8 January 2021, Rosenfeld was asked in an interview with <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Fantano" title="Anthony Fantano">Anthony Fantano</a> whether or not there was still a third volume of his music intended for release. Rosenfeld responded, saying, "I have something—I consider it finished—but things have become complicated, especially as <i>Minecraft</i> is now a big property, so I don't know."<sup id="cite_ref-Fantano-Third-Volume_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fantano-Third-Volume-218">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Variants">Variants</span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Minecraft_(franchise)" title="Minecraft (franchise)"><i>Minecraft</i> (franchise)</a></div>
<p>For the tenth anniversary of the game's release, Mojang remade a version of <i>Minecraft Classic</i> in <a href="/wiki/JavaScript" title="JavaScript">JavaScript</a> and made it available to play online.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> It functions much the same as creative mode, allowing players to build and destroy any and all parts of the world either alone or in a multiplayer server. Environmental hazards such as lava do not damage players, and some blocks function differently since their behavior was later changed during development.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Around 2011, prior to <i>Minecraft</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s full release, there had been collaboration between Mojang and <a href="/wiki/The_Lego_Group" title="The Lego Group">The Lego Group</a> to make a <a href="/wiki/Lego" title="Lego">Lego</a> brick-based <i>Minecraft</i> game to be called <i>Brickcraft</i>. This would have modified the base <i>Minecraft</i> game to use Lego bricks, which meant adapting the basic 1×1 block to account for larger pieces typically used in Lego sets. Persson had worked on the preliminary version of this game, which he had named "Project Rex Kwon Do" based on the joke from <i><a href="/wiki/Napoleon_Dynamite" title="Napoleon Dynamite">Napoleon Dynamite</a></i>. Lego had greenlit the project to go forward, and while Mojang had put two developers on the game for six months, they later opted to cancel the project, as Mojang felt that the Lego Group were too demanding on what they could do, according to Mojang's Daniel Kaplan. The Lego Group had considered buying out Mojang to complete the game, but at this point Microsoft made its offer to buy the company for over $2 billion. According to the Lego Group's Ronny Scherer, the company was not yet sure of the potential success of <i>Minecraft</i> at this point and backed off from acquisition after Microsoft brought this offer to Mojang.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Virtual_reality">Virtual reality</span></h4>
<p>Early on, Persson planned to support the <a href="/wiki/Oculus_Rift" title="Oculus Rift">Oculus Rift</a> with a port of <i>Minecraft</i>. However, after Facebook acquired Oculus in 2013, he abruptly canceled plans noting "Facebook creeps me out."<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> A community-made modification known as <i>Minecraft VR</i> was developed in 2016 to provide virtual reality support to <i>Minecraft: Java Edition</i> oriented towards Oculus Rift hardware. A <a href="/wiki/Fork_(software_development)" title="Fork (software development)">fork</a> of the <i>Minecraft VR</i> modification known as <i>Vivecraft</i> ported the mod to <a href="/wiki/OpenVR" title="OpenVR">OpenVR</a>, and is oriented towards supporting <a href="/wiki/HTC_Vive" title="HTC Vive">HTC Vive</a> hardware.<sup id="cite_ref-ars-minecriftgone_226-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ars-minecriftgone-226">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> On 15 August 2016, Microsoft launched official Oculus Rift support for <i>Minecraft</i> on Windows 10.<sup id="cite_ref-ars-minecriftgone_226-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ars-minecriftgone-226">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> Upon its release, the <i>Minecraft VR</i> mod was discontinued by its developer due to trademark complaints issued by Microsoft, and <i>Vivecraft</i> was endorsed by the community makers of the <i>Minecraft VR</i> modification due to its Rift support and being superior to the original <i>Minecraft VR</i> mod.<sup id="cite_ref-ars-minecriftgone_226-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ars-minecriftgone-226">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> Also available is a <a href="/wiki/Samsung_Gear_VR" title="Samsung Gear VR">Gear VR</a> version, titled <i>Minecraft: Gear VR Edition</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Windows_Mixed_Reality" title="Windows Mixed Reality">Windows Mixed Reality</a> support was added in 2017. On 7 September 2020, Mojang Studios announced that the PlayStation 4 version of the game would be getting <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_VR" title="PlayStation VR">PlayStation VR</a> support in the same month.<sup id="cite_ref-PSVR_228-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PSVR-228">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> The only officially supported VR versions of <i>Minecraft</i> are the <i>PlayStation 4</i> version, <i>Minecraft: Gear VR Edition</i> and <i>Minecraft for Windows 10</i> for Oculus Rift and Windows Mixed Reality headsets.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PSVR_228-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PSVR-228">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
