<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Critics">Critics</span></h3>
<p>Early versions of <i>Minecraft</i> received critical acclaim, praising the creative freedom it grants players in-game, as well as the ease of enabling <a href="/wiki/Emergent_gameplay" title="Emergent gameplay">emergent gameplay</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-PCGamerUK_258-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PCGamerUK-258">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PCPowerPlay_259-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PCPowerPlay-259">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Valve_260-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Valve-260">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup> Critics have praised <i>Minecraft</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> complex crafting system, commenting that it is an important aspect of the game's open-ended gameplay.<sup id="cite_ref-GS_review_245-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GS_review-245">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup> Most publications were impressed by the game's "blocky" graphics, with <a href="/wiki/IGN" title="IGN">IGN</a> describing them as "instantly memorable".<sup id="cite_ref-IGN_review_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IGN_review-25">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Reviewers also liked the game's adventure elements, noting that the game creates a good balance between exploring and building.<sup id="cite_ref-GS_review_245-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GS_review-245">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup> The game's multiplayer feature has been generally received favorably, with IGN commenting that "adventuring is always better with friends".<sup id="cite_ref-IGN_review_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IGN_review-25">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Jaz McDougall of <i><a href="/wiki/PC_Gamer" title="PC Gamer">PC Gamer</a></i> said <i>Minecraft</i> is "intuitively interesting and contagiously fun, with an unparalleled scope for creativity and memorable experiences".<sup id="cite_ref-PCReview_252-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PCReview-252">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup> It has been regarded as having introduced millions of children to the digital world, insofar as its basic <a href="/wiki/Game_mechanics" title="Game mechanics">game mechanics</a> are logically analogous to computer commands.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Minecraft_Generation_261-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Minecraft_Generation-261">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>IGN was disappointed about the troublesome steps needed to set up multiplayer servers, calling it a "hassle".<sup id="cite_ref-IGN_review_25-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IGN_review-25">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Critics also said that visual glitches occur periodically.<sup id="cite_ref-GS_review_245-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GS_review-245">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup> Despite its release out of beta in 2011, <a href="/wiki/GameSpot" title="GameSpot">GameSpot</a> said the game had an "unfinished feel", adding that some game elements seem "incomplete or thrown together in haste".<sup id="cite_ref-GS_review_245-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GS_review-245">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A review of the alpha version, by Scott Munro of the <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Record_(Scotland)" title="Daily Record (Scotland)">Daily Record</a></i>, called it "already something special" and urged readers to buy it.<sup id="cite_ref-DRreview_262-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DRreview-262">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jim_Rossignol" title="Jim Rossignol">Jim Rossignol</a> of <a href="/wiki/Rock_Paper_Shotgun" title="Rock Paper Shotgun">Rock Paper Shotgun</a> also recommended the alpha of the game, calling it "a kind of generative 8-bit <a href="/wiki/Lego" title="Lego">Lego</a> <i><a href="/wiki/S.T.A.L.K.E.R.:_Shadow_of_Chernobyl" title="S.T.A.L.K.E.R.: Shadow of Chernobyl">Stalker</a></i>".<sup id="cite_ref-RPSreview_263-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RPSreview-263">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup> On 17 September 2010, gaming <a href="/wiki/Webcomic" title="Webcomic">webcomic</a> <i>Penny Arcade</i> began a series of comics and news posts about the addictiveness of the game.<sup id="cite_ref-PennyArcade_264-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PennyArcade-264">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup> The Xbox 360 version was generally received positively by critics, but did not receive as much praise as the PC version. Although reviewers were disappointed by the lack of features such as mod support and content from the PC version, they acclaimed the port's addition of a tutorial and in-game tips and crafting recipes, saying that they make the game more user-friendly.<sup id="cite_ref-IGN_Xbox_96-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IGN_Xbox-96">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> The <i>Xbox One Edition</i> was one of the best received ports, being praised for its relatively large worlds.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_265-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-265">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <i>PlayStation 3 Edition</i> also received generally favorable reviews, being compared to the <i>Xbox 360 Edition</i> and praised for its well-adapted controls.<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup> The PlayStation 4 edition was the best received port to date, being praised for having 36 times larger worlds than the PlayStation 3 edition and described as nearly identical to the Xbox One edition.<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto_265-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-265">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto1_231-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-231">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup> The <i>PlayStation Vita Edition</i> received generally positive reviews from critics but was noted for its technical limitations.<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Wii U version received generally positive reviews from critics but was noted for a lack of GamePad integration.<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup> The 3DS version received mixed reviews, being criticized for its high price, technical issues, and lack of cross-platform play.<sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup> The <i>Nintendo Switch Edition</i> received fairly positive reviews from critics, being praised, like other modern ports, for its relatively larger worlds.<sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">&#91;261&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i>Minecraft: Pocket Edition</i> initially received mixed reviews from critics. Although reviewers appreciated the game's intuitive controls, they were disappointed by the lack of content. The inability to collect resources and craft items, as well as the limited types of blocks and lack of hostile mobs, were especially criticized.<sup id="cite_ref-MC_Pocket_248-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MC_Pocket-248">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup> After updates added more content, Pocket Edition started receiving more positive reviews. Reviewers complimented the controls and the graphics, but still noted a lack of content.<sup id="cite_ref-MC_Pocket_248-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MC_Pocket-248">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sales">Sales</span></h3>
<p><i>Minecraft</i> surpassed over a million purchases less than a month after entering its beta phase in early 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-usercount12012011_274-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usercount12012011-274">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-usercountblog_275-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usercountblog-275">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup> At the same time, the game had no <a href="/wiki/Video_game_publisher" title="Video game publisher">publisher</a> backing and has never been commercially advertised except through <a href="/wiki/Word_of_mouth" title="Word of mouth">word of mouth</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-noads_276-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-noads-276">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup> and various unpaid references in popular media such as the <i><a href="/wiki/Penny_Arcade" title="Penny Arcade">Penny Arcade</a></i> webcomic.<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup> By April 2011, Persson estimated that <i>Minecraft</i> had made €23 million (US$33 million) in revenue, with 800,000 sales of the alpha version of the game, and over 1 million sales of the beta version.<sup id="cite_ref-GSAprilsales_278-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GSAprilsales-278">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup> In November 2011, prior to the game's full release, <i>Minecraft</i> beta surpassed 16 million registered users and 4 million purchases.<sup id="cite_ref-sales11092011_279-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sales11092011-279">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup> By March 2012, <i>Minecraft</i> had become the 6th <a href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_PC_games" title="List of best-selling PC games">best-selling PC game</a> of all time.<sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup> As of 10&#160;October&#160;2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Minecraft&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the game had sold 17 million copies on PC, becoming the best-selling PC game of all time.<sup id="cite_ref-built_to_last_281-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-built_to_last-281">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup> On 25 February 2014, the game reached 100 million registered users.<sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">&#91;272&#93;</a></sup> By May 2019, 180 million copies had been sold across all platforms, making it the single best-selling video game of all time. The free-to-play <i>Minecraft China</i> version had over 300 million players by November 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-China-300m_283-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-China-300m-283">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup> By April 2021, <i>Minecraft</i> sold more than 238 million copies worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-:10_284-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:10-284">&#91;274&#93;</a></sup> As of 2023, the game has sold over 300 million copies.<sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Xbox 360 version of <i>Minecraft</i> became profitable within the first day of the game's release in 2012, when the game broke the Xbox Live sales records with 400,000 players online.<sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286">&#91;276&#93;</a></sup> Within a week of being on the Xbox Live Marketplace, <i>Minecraft</i> sold upwards of a million copies.<sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">&#91;277&#93;</a></sup> GameSpot announced in December 2012 that <i>Minecraft</i> sold over 4.48 million copies since the game debuted on <a href="/wiki/Xbox_Live_Arcade" title="Xbox Live Arcade">Xbox Live Arcade</a> in May 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-GSpot_–_sales_288-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GSpot_–_sales-288">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup> In 2012, <i>Minecraft</i> was the most purchased title on Xbox Live Arcade; it was also the fourth most played title on Xbox Live based on average <a href="/wiki/Unique_user" title="Unique user">unique users</a> per day.<sup id="cite_ref-xboxlive-2012_289-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xboxlive-2012-289">&#91;279&#93;</a></sup> As of 4&#160;April&#160;2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Minecraft&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the Xbox 360 version has sold 12 million copies.<sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290">&#91;280&#93;</a></sup> In addition, <i>Minecraft: Pocket Edition</i> has reached a figure of 21 million in sales.<sup id="cite_ref-291" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-291">&#91;281&#93;</a></sup> The <i>PlayStation 3 Edition</i> sold one million copies in five weeks.<sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292">&#91;282&#93;</a></sup> The release of the game's PlayStation Vita version boosted <i>Minecraft</i> sales by 79%, outselling both PS3 and PS4 debut releases and becoming the largest <i>Minecraft</i> launch on a PlayStation console.<sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">&#91;283&#93;</a></sup> The PS Vita version sold 100,000 digital copies in Japan within the first two months of release, according to an announcement by SCE Japan Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294">&#91;284&#93;</a></sup> By January 2015, 500,000 digital copies of <i>Minecraft</i> were sold in Japan across all PlayStation platforms, with a surge in primary school children purchasing the PS Vita version.<sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">&#91;285&#93;</a></sup> As of 2022, the Vita version has sold over 1.65 million physical copies in Japan, making it the best-selling Vita game in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-296" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-296">&#91;286&#93;</a></sup> <i>Minecraft</i> helped improve Microsoft's total first-party revenue by $63 million for the 2015 second quarter.<sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297">&#91;287&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The game, including all of its versions, had over 112 million monthly active players by September 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298">&#91;288&#93;</a></sup> On its 11th anniversary in May 2020, the company announced that <i>Minecraft</i> had reached over 200 million copies sold across platforms with over 126 million monthly active players.<sup id="cite_ref-:5_299-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-299">&#91;289&#93;</a></sup> By April 2021, the number of active monthly users had climbed to 140 million.<sup id="cite_ref-:9_300-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:9-300">&#91;290&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:10_284-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:10-284">&#91;274&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-301" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-301">&#91;291&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards">Awards</span></h3>
<p>In July 2010, <i>PC Gamer</i> listed <i>Minecraft</i> as the fourth-best game to play at work.<sup id="cite_ref-PCGamer_302-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PCGamer-302">&#91;292&#93;</a></sup> In December of that year, <a href="/wiki/Good_Game_(TV_program)" title="Good Game (TV program)">Good Game</a> selected <i>Minecraft</i> as their choice for Best Downloadable Game of 2010,<sup id="cite_ref-GGaward_303-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GGaward-303">&#91;293&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Game_Developer_(website)" title="Game Developer (website)">Gamasutra</a> named it the eighth best game of the year as well as the eighth best indie game of the year,<sup id="cite_ref-GSaward_304-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GSaward-304">&#91;294&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GSaward2_305-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GSaward2-305">&#91;295&#93;</a></sup> and Rock, Paper, Shotgun named it the "game of the year".<sup id="cite_ref-RPSgoty_306-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RPSgoty-306">&#91;296&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mod_DB" title="Mod DB">Indie DB</a> awarded the game the 2010 Indie of the Year award as chosen by voters, in addition to two out of five Editor's Choice awards for Most Innovative and Best Singleplayer Indie.<sup id="cite_ref-IDBaward_307-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IDBaward-307">&#91;297&#93;</a></sup> It was also awarded Game of the Year by <i>PC Gamer UK</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-PCGamerUK1_308-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PCGamerUK1-308">&#91;298&#93;</a></sup> The game was nominated for the <a href="/wiki/Seumas_McNally_Grand_Prize" title="Seumas McNally Grand Prize">Seumas McNally Grand Prize</a>, Technical Excellence, and Excellence in Design awards at the March 2011 <a href="/wiki/Independent_Games_Festival" title="Independent Games Festival">Independent Games Festival</a> and won the Grand Prize and the community-voted Audience Award.<sup id="cite_ref-IGFnoms_309-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IGFnoms-309">&#91;299&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-IGFwins_310-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IGFwins-310">&#91;300&#93;</a></sup> At <a href="/wiki/Game_Developers_Choice_Awards" title="Game Developers Choice Awards">Game Developers Choice Awards</a> 2011, <i>Minecraft</i> won awards in the categories for Best Debut Game, Best Downloadable Game and Innovation Award, winning every award for which it was nominated.<sup id="cite_ref-311" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-311">&#91;301&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-312" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-312">&#91;302&#93;</a></sup> It also won <a href="/wiki/GameCity" title="GameCity">GameCity</a>'s video game arts award.<sup id="cite_ref-313" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-313">&#91;303&#93;</a></sup> On 5 May 2011, <i>Minecraft</i> was selected as one of the 80 games that would be displayed at the <a href="/wiki/Smithsonian_American_Art_Museum" title="Smithsonian American Art Museum">Smithsonian American Art Museum</a> as part of <a href="/wiki/The_Art_of_Video_Games" title="The Art of Video Games">The Art of Video Games</a> exhibit that opened on 16 March 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-314" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-314">&#91;304&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-315" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-315">&#91;305&#93;</a></sup> At the 2011 <a href="/wiki/Spike_Video_Game_Awards" title="Spike Video Game Awards">Spike Video Game Awards</a>, <i>Minecraft</i> won the award for Best Independent Game and was nominated in the Best PC Game category.<sup id="cite_ref-spike_–_independent_316-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spike_–_independent-316">&#91;306&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-spike_–_pc_317-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spike_–_pc-317">&#91;307&#93;</a></sup> In 2012, at the <a href="/wiki/British_Academy_Games_Awards" title="British Academy Games Awards">British Academy Video Games Awards</a>, <i>Minecraft</i> was nominated in the GAME Award of 2011 category and Persson received The Special Award.<sup id="cite_ref-bafta_318-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bafta-318">&#91;308&#93;</a></sup> In 2012, <i>Minecraft</i> XBLA was awarded a <a href="/wiki/Golden_Joystick_Awards" title="Golden Joystick Awards">Golden Joystick Award</a> in the Best Downloadable Game category,<sup id="cite_ref-CVG_Golden_Joystick_319-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CVG_Golden_Joystick-319">&#91;309&#93;</a></sup> and a <a href="/wiki/The_Independent_Game_Developers%27_Association" title="The Independent Game Developers&#39; Association">TIGA</a> Games Industry Award in the Best Arcade Game category.<sup id="cite_ref-320" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-320">&#91;310&#93;</a></sup> In 2013, it was nominated as the family game of the year at the British Academy Video Games Awards.<sup id="cite_ref-321" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-321">&#91;311&#93;</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/16th_Annual_D.I.C.E._Awards" title="16th Annual D.I.C.E. Awards">16th Annual D.I.C.E. Awards</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Interactive_Arts_%26_Sciences" title="Academy of Interactive Arts &amp; Sciences">Academy of Interactive Arts &amp; Sciences</a> nominated the Xbox 360 version of <i>Minecraft</i> for "<a href="/wiki/D.I.C.E._Award_for_Strategy/Simulation_Game_of_the_Year" title="D.I.C.E. Award for Strategy/Simulation Game of the Year">Strategy/Simulation Game of the Year</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-322" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-322">&#91;312&#93;</a></sup> <i>Minecraft Console Edition</i> won the award for TIGA Game Of The Year in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-323" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-323">&#91;313&#93;</a></sup> In 2015, the game placed 6th on <i><a href="/wiki/Eurogamer#Subsidiaries" title="Eurogamer">USgamer</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> The 15 Best Games Since 2000 list.<sup id="cite_ref-324" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-324">&#91;314&#93;</a></sup> In 2016, <i>Minecraft</i> placed 6th on <a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a>'s The 50 Best Video Games of All Time list.<sup id="cite_ref-325" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-325">&#91;315&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i>Minecraft</i> was nominated for the <a href="/wiki/2013_Kids%27_Choice_Awards" title="2013 Kids&#39; Choice Awards">2013 Kids' Choice Awards</a> for <a href="/wiki/Kids%27_Choice_Award_for_Favorite_Video_Game#Favorite_App" title="Kids&#39; Choice Award for Favorite Video Game">Favorite App</a>, but lost to <i><a href="/wiki/Temple_Run" title="Temple Run">Temple Run</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-326" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-326">&#91;316&#93;</a></sup> It was nominated for the <a href="/wiki/2014_Kids%27_Choice_Awards" title="2014 Kids&#39; Choice Awards">2014 Kids' Choice Awards</a> for <a href="/wiki/Kids%27_Choice_Award_for_Favorite_Video_Game" title="Kids&#39; Choice Award for Favorite Video Game">Favorite Video Game</a>, but lost to <i><a href="/wiki/Just_Dance_2014" title="Just Dance 2014">Just Dance 2014</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-327" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-327">&#91;317&#93;</a></sup> The game later won the award for the Most Addicting Game at the <a href="/wiki/2015_Kids%27_Choice_Awards" title="2015 Kids&#39; Choice Awards">2015 Kids' Choice Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-328" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-328">&#91;318&#93;</a></sup> In addition, the <i>Java Edition</i> was nominated for "Favorite Video Game" at the <a href="/wiki/2018_Kids%27_Choice_Awards" title="2018 Kids&#39; Choice Awards">2018 Kids' Choice Awards</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-329" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-329">&#91;319&#93;</a></sup> while the game itself won the "Still Playing" award at the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Joystick_Awards#2019" title="Golden Joystick Awards">2019 Golden Joystick Awards</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-330" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-330">&#91;320&#93;</a></sup> as well as the "Favorite Video Game" award at the <a href="/wiki/2020_Kids%27_Choice_Awards" title="2020 Kids&#39; Choice Awards">2020 Kids' Choice Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-331" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-331">&#91;321&#93;</a></sup> <i>Minecraft</i> also won "Stream Game of the Year" at inaugural <a href="/wiki/The_Streamer_Awards" title="The Streamer Awards">Streamer Awards</a> in 2022.<sup id="cite_ref-332" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-332">&#91;322&#93;</a></sup> The game later garnered a <a href="/wiki/Nickelodeon_Kids%27_Choice_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Nickelodeon Kids&#39; Choice Award">Nickelodeon Kids' Choice Award</a> nomination for Favorite Video Game in <a href="/wiki/2021_Kids%27_Choice_Awards" title="2021 Kids&#39; Choice Awards">2021</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-333" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-333">&#91;323&#93;</a></sup> and won the same category in <a href="/wiki/2022_Kids%27_Choice_Awards" title="2022 Kids&#39; Choice Awards">2022</a> and <a href="/wiki/2023_Kids%27_Choice_Awards" title="2023 Kids&#39; Choice Awards">2023</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-334" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-334">&#91;324&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-335" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-335">&#91;325&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversies">Controversies</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2014_EULA_changes">2014 EULA changes</span></h4>
<p>Microsoft and Mojang announced in June 2014 that it would be changing the <i>Minecraft</i> <a href="/wiki/End-user_license_agreement" title="End-user license agreement">end-user license agreement</a> (EULA) to prohibit servers from accepting donations or payments in exchange for the donating or paying players receiving in-game advantages on such server, essentially banning servers from enacting "<a href="/wiki/Free-to-play" title="Free-to-play">pay-to-win</a>" (PTW) servers. Mojang spokesperson Owen Hill provided examples of what it would and would not allow, saying company would allow for pay-to-play servers in which a player is required to pay a fee to access the server, or for cosmetic enhancements (such as in-game costumes or pets), but that Mojang would be cracking down on paying to obtain powerful swords or potions (providing a competitive advantage to the player versus other players). The new crackdowns were supported by Persson, citing him receiving multiple emails from parents of children who had spent hundreds of dollars on servers. The <i>Minecraft</i> community and server owners, however, heavily despised the new change in enforcement and protested en masse, which included comparing Mojang to monolithic video game publishers like <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Arts" title="Electronic Arts">Electronic Arts</a> and <a href="/wiki/Activision" title="Activision">Activision</a>, gaming companies often criticized online for their highly restrictive digital rights management and user license agreements. Many argued that the crackdown would force smaller servers to close their doors, and some blamed the crackdown on Mojang attempting to suppress competition for its own <i>Minecraft Realms</i> subscription service.<sup id="cite_ref-336" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-336">&#91;326&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Account_migration">Account migration</span></h4>
<p>In 2020, Mojang Studios revealed that it would begin the process of requiring that <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_account" title="Microsoft account">Microsoft accounts</a> be used in order to log into the <i>Java Edition</i> of the game, and that older Mojang Studios accounts would be sunsetted. The move to Microsoft accounts also required <i>Java Edition</i> players to create <a href="/wiki/Xbox_network" title="Xbox network">Xbox network</a> Gamertags. Mojang Studios defended the move to Microsoft accounts by saying that improved security could be offered, which included Java accounts being able to use <a href="/wiki/Multi-factor_authentication" title="Multi-factor authentication">two factor authentication</a>, players could block cyberbullies in chat, and improve parental controls. The community responded with intense backlash against this announcement, particularly taking issue to the various technical difficulties encountered in the process and how account migration would be mandatory, even for those who do not play on servers. As of 10 March 2022, Microsoft required that all players migrate in order to access the <i>Java Edition</i> of <i>Minecraft</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-337" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-337">&#91;327&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-338" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-338">&#91;328&#93;</a></sup> A deadline of 19 September 2023 was announced to complete account migration, after which all legacy Mojang accounts became inaccessible and unable to be migrated.<sup id="cite_ref-339" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-339">&#91;329&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><span class="anchor" id="saveminecraft"></span>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Java_Edition_chat_reporting"><i>Java Edition</i> chat reporting</span></h4>
<p>In June 2022, Microsoft and Mojang Studios announced it would be releasing a player reporting feature in all future builds of <i>Java Edition</i>. In earlier development builds, players could report other players on multiplayer servers for sending messages that are prohibited by the Xbox Live Code of Conduct; report categories included profane language, substance abuse, hate speech, threats of violence, and nudity, though Microsoft in later builds has since excluded the profane language category from the player reporting feature. If a player was found to be in violation of Xbox Community Standards, the player would be banned from all servers for a specific period of time or permanently. The update containing the report feature (1.19.1) was released on 27 July 2022.<sup id="cite_ref-340" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-340">&#91;330&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Microsoft and Mojang Studios received substantial backlash and protest from community members, one of the most common complaints being that banned players would be forbidden from joining any server, even private ones. Others took issue to what they saw as Microsoft increasing control over its player base and exercising censorship,<sup id="cite_ref-341" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-341">&#91;331&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-342" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-342">&#91;332&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-343" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-343">&#91;333&#93;</a></sup> sparking some to dub the version "1.19.84", in reference to the novel <i><a href="/wiki/Nineteen_Eighty-Four" title="Nineteen Eighty-Four">Nineteen Eighty-Four</a></i>, which deals with similar themes of censorship.<sup id="cite_ref-344" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-344">&#91;334&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-345" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-345">&#91;335&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><span class="anchor" id="Popular_culture_and_social_media"></span>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_impact">Cultural impact</span></h2>
<p>In September 2019, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> classified <i>Minecraft</i> as the best video game of (the first two decades of) the 21st century,<sup id="cite_ref-346" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-346">&#91;336&#93;</a></sup> and in November 2019
<i><a href="/wiki/Polygon_(website)" title="Polygon (website)">Polygon</a></i> called the game the "most important game of the decade" in its 2010s "decade in review".<sup id="cite_ref-347" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-347">&#91;337&#93;</a></sup> In December 2019, <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> gave <i>Minecraft</i> a special mention in a list of the best video games of the 2010s, stating that the game is "without a doubt one of the most important games of the last ten years."<sup id="cite_ref-forbes_348-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forbes-348">&#91;338&#93;</a></sup> In June 2020, <i>Minecraft</i> was inducted into the <a href="/wiki/World_Video_Game_Hall_of_Fame" title="World Video Game Hall of Fame">World Video Game Hall of Fame</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:6_349-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:6-349">&#91;339&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i>Minecraft</i> is recognized as one of the first successful games to use an <a href="/wiki/Early_access" title="Early access">early access</a> model to draw in sales prior to its full release version to help fund development.<sup id="cite_ref-350" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-350">&#91;340&#93;</a></sup> As <i>Minecraft</i> helped to bolster indie game development in the early 2010s, it also helped to popularize the use of the early access model in indie game development.<sup id="cite_ref-gamasutra_351-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gamasutra-351">&#91;341&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Jordan_Maron_headshot_2018.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Jordan_Maron_headshot_2018.jpg/175px-Jordan_Maron_headshot_2018.jpg" decoding="async" width="175" height="175" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Jordan_Maron_headshot_2018.jpg/263px-Jordan_Maron_headshot_2018.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Jordan_Maron_headshot_2018.jpg/350px-Jordan_Maron_headshot_2018.jpg 2x" data-file-width="831" data-file-height="831" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Jordan_Maron" class="mw-redirect" title="Jordan Maron">Jordan Maron</a> (known professionally as "CaptainSparklez") is known for his musical <i>Minecraft</i> parodies of popular songs.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Social media sites such as <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a>, <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Reddit" title="Reddit">Reddit</a> have played a significant role in popularizing <i>Minecraft</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Social_media_352-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Social_media-352">&#91;342&#93;</a></sup> Research conducted by the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pennsylvania" title="University of Pennsylvania">University of Pennsylvania</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Annenberg_School_for_Communication_at_the_University_of_Pennsylvania" title="Annenberg School for Communication at the University of Pennsylvania">Annenberg School of Communication</a> showed that one-third of <i>Minecraft</i> players learned about the game via Internet videos.<sup id="cite_ref-353" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-353">&#91;343&#93;</a></sup> In 2010, <i>Minecraft</i>-related videos began to gain influence on YouTube, often made by commentators. The videos usually contain screen-capture footage of the game and voice-overs.<sup id="cite_ref-salon_354-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-salon-354">&#91;344&#93;</a></sup> Common coverage in the videos includes creations made by players, <a href="/wiki/Strategy_guide" title="Strategy guide">walkthroughs</a> of various tasks, and parodies of works in popular culture. By May 2012, over four million <i>Minecraft</i>-related YouTube videos had been uploaded.<sup id="cite_ref-Merchandise_sales_355-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Merchandise_sales-355">&#91;345&#93;</a></sup> The game would go on to be a prominent fixture within YouTube's gaming scene during the entire 2010s; in 2014, it was the second-most searched term on the entire platform.<sup id="cite_ref-Alexander2019_356-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alexander2019-356">&#91;346&#93;</a></sup> By 2018, it was still YouTube's biggest game globally.<sup id="cite_ref-357" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-357">&#91;347&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Some popular commentators have received employment at <a href="/wiki/Machinima,_Inc." title="Machinima, Inc.">Machinima</a>, a gaming video company that owns a highly watched entertainment channel on YouTube.<sup id="cite_ref-salon_354-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-salon-354">&#91;344&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/The_Yogscast" class="mw-redirect" title="The Yogscast">The Yogscast</a> is a British company that regularly produces <i>Minecraft</i> videos; their YouTube channel has attained billions of views, and their panel at <a href="/wiki/Minecon#2011" title="Minecon">Minecon 2011</a> had the highest attendance.<sup id="cite_ref-salon_354-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-salon-354">&#91;344&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bbc_tycoons_358-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc_tycoons-358">&#91;348&#93;</a></sup> Other well-known YouTube personalities include <a href="/wiki/Jordan_Maron" class="mw-redirect" title="Jordan Maron">Jordan Maron</a>, who has created many <i>Minecraft</i> <a href="/wiki/Parody" title="Parody">parodies</a>, including "Minecraft Style", a parody of the internationally successful single "<a href="/wiki/Gangnam_Style" title="Gangnam Style">Gangnam Style</a>" by South Korean rapper <a href="/wiki/Psy" title="Psy">Psy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Minecraft_Style_359-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Minecraft_Style-359">&#91;349&#93;</a></sup> <i>Minecraft</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s popularity on YouTube was described by <i><a href="/wiki/Polygon_(website)" title="Polygon (website)">Polygon</a></i> as quietly dominant, although in 2019, thanks in part to <a href="/wiki/PewDiePie" title="PewDiePie">PewDiePie</a>'s playthroughs of the game, <i>Minecraft</i> experienced a visible uptick in popularity on the platform.<sup id="cite_ref-Alexander2019_356-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alexander2019-356">&#91;346&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hernandez2019_360-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hernandez2019-360">&#91;350&#93;</a></sup> YouTube later announced that on 14 December 2021 that the total amount of <i>Minecraft</i>-related views exceeded one trillion since the game's inception in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-361" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-361">&#91;351&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i>Minecraft</i> has been referenced by other video games, such as <i><a href="/wiki/Torchlight_II" title="Torchlight II">Torchlight II</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Team_Fortress_2" title="Team Fortress 2">Team Fortress 2</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-362" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-362">&#91;352&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-363" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-363">&#91;353&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Borderlands_2" title="Borderlands 2">Borderlands 2</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Choplifter_HD" title="Choplifter HD">Choplifter HD</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Super_Meat_Boy" title="Super Meat Boy">Super Meat Boy</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Elder_Scrolls_V:_Skyrim" title="The Elder Scrolls V: Skyrim">The Elder Scrolls V: Skyrim</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Binding_of_Isaac_(video_game)" title="The Binding of Isaac (video game)">The Binding of Isaac</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Stanley_Parable" title="The Stanley Parable">The Stanley Parable</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/FTL:_Faster_Than_Light" title="FTL: Faster Than Light">FTL: Faster Than Light</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-364" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-364">&#91;354&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-365" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-365">&#91;355&#93;</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/Super_Smash_Bros._Ultimate" title="Super Smash Bros. Ultimate">Super Smash Bros. Ultimate</a></i>, the lattermost of which features a downloadable character and stage based on <i>Minecraft</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-366" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-366">&#91;356&#93;</a></sup> It was also referenced by electronic music artist <a href="/wiki/Deadmau5" title="Deadmau5">deadmau5</a> in his performances.<sup id="cite_ref-367" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-367">&#91;357&#93;</a></sup> The game is also referenced heavily in "<a href="/wiki/Informative_Murder_Porn" title="Informative Murder Porn">Informative Murder Porn</a>", the second episode of the <a href="/wiki/South_Park_(season_17)" title="South Park (season 17)">seventeenth season</a> of the animated television series <i><a href="/wiki/South_Park" title="South Park">South Park</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-368" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-368">&#91;358&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Applications">Applications</span></h3>
<p>The possible applications of <i>Minecraft</i> have been discussed extensively, especially in the fields of <a href="/wiki/Computer-aided_design" title="Computer-aided design">computer-aided design</a> (CAD) and education. In a panel at Minecon 2011, a Swedish developer discussed the possibility of using the game to redesign public buildings and parks, stating that rendering using <i>Minecraft</i> was much more user-friendly for the community, making it easier to envision the functionality of new buildings and parks.<sup id="cite_ref-salon_354-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-salon-354">&#91;344&#93;</a></sup> In 2012, a member of the <a href="/wiki/Human_dynamics" title="Human dynamics">Human Dynamics</a> group at the <a href="/wiki/MIT_Media_Lab" title="MIT Media Lab">MIT Media Lab</a>, Cody Sumter, said: "Notch hasn't just built a game. He's tricked 40 million people into learning to use a CAD program." Various software has been developed to allow virtual designs to be printed using professional <a href="/wiki/3D_printing" title="3D printing">3D printers</a> or personal printers such as <a href="/wiki/MakerBot" title="MakerBot">MakerBot</a> and <a href="/wiki/RepRap" title="RepRap">RepRap</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-369" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-369">&#91;359&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2012, Mojang began the <i><a href="/wiki/Block_by_Block_(program)" title="Block by Block (program)">Block by Block</a></i> project in cooperation with <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Human_Settlements_Programme" title="United Nations Human Settlements Programme">UN Habitat</a> to create real-world environments in <i>Minecraft</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-370" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-370">&#91;360&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-371" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-371">&#91;361&#93;</a></sup> The project allows young people who live in those environments to participate in designing the changes they would like to see. Using <i>Minecraft</i>, the community has helped reconstruct the areas of concern, and citizens are invited to enter the <i>Minecraft</i> servers and modify their own neighborhood. Carl Manneh, Mojang's managing director, called the game "the perfect tool to facilitate this process", adding "The three-year partnership will support UN-Habitat's Sustainable Urban Development Network to upgrade 300 public spaces by 2016." Mojang signed <i>Minecraft</i> building community, <i>FyreUK</i>, to help render the environments into <i>Minecraft</i>. The first pilot project began in <a href="/wiki/Kibera" title="Kibera">Kibera</a>, one of <a href="/wiki/Nairobi" title="Nairobi">Nairobi</a>'s informal settlements and is in the planning phase. The <i>Block by Block</i> project is based on an earlier initiative started in October 2011, <i>Mina Kvarter</i> (My Block), which gave young people in Swedish communities a tool to visualize how they wanted to change their part of town. According to Manneh, the project was a helpful way to visualize urban planning ideas without necessarily having a training in architecture. The ideas presented by the citizens were a template for political decisions.<sup id="cite_ref-372" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-372">&#91;362&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-blockbyblock_373-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-blockbyblock-373">&#91;363&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Minecraft_sheep_(11453641143).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Minecraft_sheep_%2811453641143%29.jpg/187px-Minecraft_sheep_%2811453641143%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="187" height="204" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Minecraft_sheep_%2811453641143%29.jpg/281px-Minecraft_sheep_%2811453641143%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Minecraft_sheep_%2811453641143%29.jpg/375px-Minecraft_sheep_%2811453641143%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1616" data-file-height="1758" /></a><figcaption>A yarn <i>Minecraft</i> sheep</figcaption></figure>
<p>In April 2014, the <a href="/wiki/Danish_Geodata_Agency" title="Danish Geodata Agency">Danish Geodata Agency</a> generated all of Denmark in fullscale in <i>Minecraft</i> based on their own <a href="/wiki/Geographic_data_and_information" title="Geographic data and information">geodata</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DenmarkInMinecraft_374-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DenmarkInMinecraft-374">&#91;364&#93;</a></sup> This is possible because Denmark is <a href="/wiki/List_of_elevation_extremes_by_country" title="List of elevation extremes by country">one of the flattest countries</a> with the highest point at 171 meters (ranking as the country with the 30th smallest elevation span), where the limit in default Minecraft was around 192 meters above in-game sea level when the project was completed.<sup id="cite_ref-375" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-375">&#91;365&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-376" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-376">&#91;366&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Taking advantage of the game's accessibility where other websites are censored, the non-governmental organization <a href="/wiki/Reporters_Without_Borders" title="Reporters Without Borders">Reporters Without Borders</a> has used an open <i>Minecraft</i> server to create <a href="/wiki/The_Uncensored_Library" title="The Uncensored Library">the Uncensored Library</a>, a repository within the game of journalism by authors from countries (including Egypt, Mexico, Russia, Saudi Arabia and Vietnam) who have been censored and arrested, such as <a href="/wiki/Jamal_Khashoggi" title="Jamal Khashoggi">Jamal Khashoggi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-377" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-377">&#91;367&#93;</a></sup> The neoclassical virtual building was created over about 250 hours by an international team of 24 people.<sup id="cite_ref-378" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-378">&#91;368&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Despite its unpredictable nature, <i>Minecraft</i> has become a popular game for <a href="/wiki/Speedrunning" title="Speedrunning">speedrunning</a>, where players time themselves from being dropped into a new world to reaching The End and defeating the Ender Dragon boss. Some speedrunners use a combination of mods, external programs, and debug menus, while other runners play the game in a more vanilla or more consistency-oriented way.<sup id="cite_ref-379" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-379">&#91;369&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-380" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-380">&#91;370&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h4>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Minecraft_in_school.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Minecraft_in_school.jpg/247px-Minecraft_in_school.jpg" decoding="async" width="247" height="185" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Minecraft_in_school.jpg/371px-Minecraft_in_school.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Minecraft_in_school.jpg/494px-Minecraft_in_school.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a><figcaption><i>Minecraft</i> being played in an educational setting</figcaption></figure>
<p><i>Minecraft</i> has also been used in educational settings.<sup id="cite_ref-Education_381-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Education-381">&#91;371&#93;</a></sup> In 2011, an educational organization named MinecraftEdu was formed with the goal of introducing <i>Minecraft</i> into schools. The group works with Mojang to make the game affordable and accessible to schools. The version of <i>Minecraft</i> through MinecraftEdu includes unique features to allow teachers to monitor the students' progress within the virtual world, such as receiving screenshots from students to show completion of a lesson.<sup id="cite_ref-pcgamer_edu_2019_382-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pcgamer_edu_2019-382">&#91;372&#93;</a></sup> In September 2012, MinecraftEdu said that approximately 250,000 students around the world have access to <i>Minecraft</i> through the company.<sup id="cite_ref-MCEdu_383-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MCEdu-383">&#91;373&#93;</a></sup> A wide variety of educational activities involving the game have been developed to teach students various subjects, including history, language arts and science. For an example, one teacher built a world consisting of various historical landmarks for students to learn and explore.<sup id="cite_ref-MCEdu_383-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MCEdu-383">&#91;373&#93;</a></sup> Another teacher created a large-scale representation of an animal <a href="/wiki/Cell_(biology)" title="Cell (biology)">cell</a> within <i>Minecraft</i> that student could explore and learn how cell functions work.<sup id="cite_ref-pcgamer_edu_2019_382-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pcgamer_edu_2019-382">&#91;372&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Great_Ormond_Street_Hospital" title="Great Ormond Street Hospital">Great Ormond Street Hospital</a> has been recreated in <i>Minecraft</i>, and it proposed that patients can use it to virtually explore the hospital before they visit it in real life.<sup id="cite_ref-384" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-384">&#91;374&#93;</a></sup> <i>Minecraft</i> may also prove as an innovation in computer-aided design.<sup id="cite_ref-385" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-385">&#91;375&#93;</a></sup> <i>Minecraft</i> offers an outlet of collaboration in design and could have an impact on the industry.<sup id="cite_ref-386" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-386">&#91;376&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>With the introduction of redstone blocks to represent electrical circuits, users have been able to build functional virtual computers within <i>Minecraft</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-387" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-387">&#91;377&#93;</a></sup> Such virtual creations include a working <a href="/wiki/Hard_disk_drive" title="Hard disk drive">hard drive</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-388" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-388">&#91;378&#93;</a></sup> an 8-bit virtual computer,<sup id="cite_ref-389" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-389">&#91;379&#93;</a></sup> and even a smaller-scale version of <i>Minecraft</i> that is playable and able to be built completely in survival mode with no external modifications.<sup id="cite_ref-390" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-390">&#91;380&#93;</a></sup> In at least one instance, a mod has been created to use this feature to teach younger players how to program within a language set by a virtual computer within a <i>Minecraft</i> world.<sup id="cite_ref-391" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-391">&#91;381&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Another computational mechanic in <i>Minecraft</i> is the command block, a block that is only accessible in creative mode and can alter game logic. It has been used to create emulators for the <a href="/wiki/Atari_2600" title="Atari 2600">Atari 2600</a> (including one by YouTube personality <a href="/wiki/SethBling" title="SethBling">SethBling</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-392" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-392">&#91;382&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-393" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-393">&#91;383&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Game_Boy_Advance" title="Game Boy Advance">Game Boy Advance</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-394" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-394">&#91;384&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2014, the <a href="/wiki/British_Museum" title="British Museum">British Museum</a> in London announced plans to recreate its building along with all exhibits in <i>Minecraft</i> in conjunction with members of the public.<sup id="cite_ref-395" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-395">&#91;385&#93;</a></sup> Microsoft and the non-profit organisation <a href="/wiki/Code.org" title="Code.org">Code.org</a> had teamed up to offer <i>Minecraft</i>-based games, puzzles, and tutorials aimed to help teach children how to program; by March 2018, Microsoft and Code.org reported that more than 85 million children have used their tutorials.<sup id="cite_ref-396" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-396">&#91;386&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Clones">Clones</span></h3>
<p>Following the initual surge in popularity of <i>Minecraft</i> in 2010, other video games were criticised for having various similarities to <i>Minecraft</i>, and some were described as being "<a href="/wiki/Video_game_clone" title="Video game clone">clones</a>", often due to a direct inspiration from <i>Minecraft</i>, or only a superficial similarity. Examples include <i><a href="/wiki/Ace_of_Spades_(video_game)" title="Ace of Spades (video game)">Ace of Spades</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/CastleMiner" title="CastleMiner">CastleMiner</a></i>, <i>CraftWorld</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/FortressCraft" title="FortressCraft">FortressCraft</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Terraria" title="Terraria">Terraria</a></i>, <i>BlockWorld 3D</i>, <i>Total Miner</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-397" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-397">&#91;387&#93;</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/Minetest" title="Minetest">Minetest</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-398" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-398">&#91;388&#93;</a></sup> David Frampton, designer of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Blockheads_(video_game)" title="The Blockheads (video game)">The Blockheads</a></i>, reported that one failure of his 2D game was the "low resolution pixel art" that too closely resembled the art in <i>Minecraft</i>, which resulted in "some resistance" from fans.<sup id="cite_ref-FramptonPostMort_399-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FramptonPostMort-399">&#91;389&#93;</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Homebrew_(video_games)" title="Homebrew (video games)">homebrew</a> adaptation of the alpha version of <i>Minecraft</i> for the <a href="/wiki/Nintendo_DS" title="Nintendo DS">Nintendo DS</a>, titled <i>DScraft</i>, has been released; it has been noted for its similarity to the original game considering the technical limitations of the system.<sup id="cite_ref-400" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-400">&#91;390&#93;</a></sup> In response to Microsoft's acquisition of Mojang and their <i>Minecraft</i> IP, various developers announced further clone titles developed specifically for Nintendo's consoles, as they were the only major platforms to not officially receive <i>Minecraft</i> at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-NLcitesMinecraftWiiURumours_401-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NLcitesMinecraftWiiURumours-401">&#91;391&#93;</a></sup> These clone titles include <i>UCraft</i> (Nexis Games),<sup id="cite_ref-NLcitesUCraft_402-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NLcitesUCraft-402">&#91;392&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Cube_Life:_Island_Survival" title="Cube Life: Island Survival">Cube Life: Island Survival</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/Cypronia" title="Cypronia">Cypronia</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-NLcitesCLIS_403-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NLcitesCLIS-403">&#91;393&#93;</a></sup> <i>Discovery</i> (Noowanda),<sup id="cite_ref-NLcitesDiscovery_404-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NLcitesDiscovery-404">&#91;394&#93;</a></sup> <i>Battleminer</i> (Wobbly Tooth Games),<sup id="cite_ref-NLcitesBattleminer_405-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NLcitesBattleminer-405">&#91;395&#93;</a></sup> <i>Cube Creator 3D</i> (Big John Games),<sup id="cite_ref-NLcitesCubeCreator3D_406-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NLcitesCubeCreator3D-406">&#91;396&#93;</a></sup> and <i>Stone Shire</i> (Finger Gun Games).<sup id="cite_ref-NLcitesStoneShire_407-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NLcitesStoneShire-407">&#91;397&#93;</a></sup> Despite this, the fears of fans were unfounded, with official <i>Minecraft</i> releases on Nintendo consoles eventually resuming.<sup id="cite_ref-MCV-UK_interview_408-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MCV-UK_interview-408">&#91;398&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-VergecitesMSMonWiiU_409-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VergecitesMSMonWiiU-409">&#91;399&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-WiiU_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WiiU-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Markus Persson made another similar game, <i><a href="/wiki/Minicraft" title="Minicraft">Minicraft</a></i>, for a <a href="/wiki/Ludum_Dare" title="Ludum Dare">Ludum Dare</a> competition in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-410" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-410">&#91;400&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Minecon">Minecon</span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Minecon" title="Minecon">Minecon</a></div>
<p>Minecon is the annual official <a href="/wiki/Fan_convention" title="Fan convention">fan convention</a> dedicated to <i>Minecraft</i>. The first Minecon was held in November 2011 at the <a href="/wiki/Mandalay_Bay" title="Mandalay Bay">Mandalay Bay</a> Hotel and Casino in <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas" title="Las Vegas">Las Vegas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-411" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-411">&#91;401&#93;</a></sup> The event included the official launch of <i>Minecraft</i>; keynote speeches, including one by Persson; building and costume contests; <i>Minecraft</i>-themed breakout classes; exhibits by leading gaming and <i>Minecraft</i>-related companies; commemorative merchandise; and autograph and picture times with Mojang employees and well-known contributors from the <i>Minecraft</i> community.<sup id="cite_ref-412" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-412">&#91;402&#93;</a></sup> In 2016, Minecon was held in-person for the last time, with the following years featuring annual livestreams instead.
</p>

</li>
<li id="cite_note-32"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-32">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">An "infinite" world is 60 million by 60 million blocks.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-36"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-36">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In a blog post,<sup id="cite_ref-NotchExplain1_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NotchExplain1-33">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Persson explains:

<dl><dd><dl><dd>"... let me clarify some things about the "infinite" maps: They're not infinite, but there's no hard limit either. It'll just get <a href="/wiki/Software_bug" title="Software bug">buggier</a> and buggier the further out you are. Terrain is generated, saved and loaded, and (kind of) rendered in chunks of 16*16*128 blocks. These chunks have an <a href="/wiki/Offset_(computer_science)" title="Offset (computer science)">offset</a> value that is a <a href="/wiki/32-bit" class="mw-redirect" title="32-bit">32 bit</a> <a href="/wiki/Integer" title="Integer">integer</a> roughly in the range negative two billion to positive two billion. If you go outside that range (about 25% of the distance from where you are now to the sun), loading and saving chunks will start overwriting old chunks. At a 16/th of that distance, things that use integers for block positions, such as using items and pathfinding, will start <a href="/wiki/Arithmetic_overflow" class="mw-redirect" title="Arithmetic overflow">overflowing</a> and acting weird.</dd>
<dd>Those are the two "hard" limits."</dd></dl></dd></dl>
</span></li>
</ol></div></div>
